\chapter{Chiral Hochschild cohomology and Koszul duality}
\label{chap:deformation-theory}

\index{deformation theory!chiral|textbf}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!chiral|textbf}
\index{three Hochschild theories!discipline}

\begin{remark}[Hochschild register discipline]
\label{rem:three-hochschild-discipline}

The word \emph{Hochschild} denotes different complexes with different
source categories. This chapter uses the curve-level chiral
Hochschild cochain complex $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$, the tangent complex of
the chiral MC moduli on a curve. For a PBW chiral Koszul algebra with
the $E_\infty$-chiral completion and generic/perfectness hypotheses
stated in Theorem~H, it has cohomological amplitude~$[0,2]$.
It is distinct from:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item the topological Hochschild homology $\mathrm{THH}(R)$ of an
 $E_1$-ring spectrum~$R$, whose output is an $S^1$-equivariant
 spectrum;
\item the categorical Hochschild cohomology
 $\mathrm{HH}^*_{\mathrm{cat}}(\mathcal C)$ of a dg or CY category,
 whose output is an $E_2$-algebra carrying the categorical shifted
 Poisson structure;
\item the classical Hochschild complex
 $\HH^*(A_{\mathrm{mode}},A_{\mathrm{mode}})$ of the associative
 mode algebra, whose inner derivations and finiteness properties are
 those of $A_{\mathrm{mode}}$, not of the vertex-algebra zero-mode
 calculus;
\item the chiral coHochschild chain complex of a chiral coalgebra,
 which has the opposite variance. In the ordered associative
 comparison it is
$\operatorname{Cotor}^{C^e}(C_\Delta,N)$, not
$R\operatorname{Hom}_{\cA^e}(\cA,\cA)$.
\end{enumerate}
The geometry determines the register: a curve $X$ produces
$\ChirHoch$, an $E_1$-ring spectrum produces $\mathrm{THH}$, a CY dg
category produces $\mathrm{HH}_{\mathrm{cat}}$, and an associative
mode algebra produces classical $\HH$. Comparisons require the named
maps below. Throughout this chapter unqualified ``Hochschild'' means
$\ChirHoch^*$.
\end{remark}

The MC element $\Theta_\cA \in \MC(\gAmod)$ controls all of chiral
Koszul duality, but how rigid is the moduli it lives in? Without
knowing the tangent complex to
$\MC(\gAmod)/\mathrm{gauge}$, every deformation, obstruction, and
closed-sector action remains inaccessible. The chiral Hochschild
complex $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$ is that tangent complex. Theorem~H is
the PBW-completed curve-level statement: on the generic chiral
Koszul locus, after the $E_\infty$ averaging hypothesis, it gives
cohomological amplitude~$[0,2]$ and the Verdier duality
\[
\ChirHoch^n(\cA)
\cong
\ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee \otimes \omega_X .
\]
No such conclusion is asserted for topological Hochschild,
categorical Hochschild, critical affine level, or non-generic
class-\(\mathsf M\) simple quotients. The amplitude is the output
of the Koszul Reflection
$K^{2}\simeq\mathrm{id}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-reflection}) read on the chiral derived
centre $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA) = \ChirHoch^*(\cA,\cA)$:
the curve dimension $\dim_\mathbb{C} X = 1$ contributes the curve
amplitude $[0,1]$, the bigraded Verdier shift contributes the extra
$[1]$, and PBW Koszul collapse forces the diagonal to be the only
contributing direction. The structural source of this
amplitude~$[0,2]$ is the curve-level chiral brace/Gerstenhaber
structure on $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ together with PBW
collapse and completion. No $E_3$ upgrade, CY-$d$ product ambient,
topological Hochschild theorem, or categorical Hochschild
concentration is used in Theorem~H.

The cyclic deformation complex $\Defcyc(\cA)$
(Definition~\ref{def:cyclic-deformation-elementary}) is the cyclic
refinement of $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$.
The complementarity
theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}) identifies
the $\cA$-visible and $\cA^!$-visible tangent directions as
complementary Lagrangians in the shifted-symplectic MC moduli.

The chiral Hochschild complexes
carry natural brace and $E_2$ structures. The convolution dg~Lie
algebra $\Convstr(\barB(\cA), \cA)$ governing deformations is the
strict model of the $L_\infty$ deformation object
$\Convinf(\barB(\cA), \cA)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:operadic-homotopy-convolution}).
The modular cyclic deformation complex
$\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-cyclic-deformation-complex}),
strict model of $\Definfmod(\cA)$
(Remark~\ref{rem:modular-cyc-strictification}),
extends these structures to the full modular regime.

Two algebraic objects govern the open/closed dictionary:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Bar/cobar} classifies \emph{twisting morphisms}:
 maps from a conilpotent coalgebra into a chiral algebra, equivalently
 maps out of the corresponding cobar algebra
 (Chapter~\ref{chap:bar-cobar}). For~$\cA$ itself this gives the
 inversion $\Omega\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\simeq \cA$. The Koszul
 dual algebra $\cA^!$ enters only after taking
 $\cA^i=H^*(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA))$ and applying Verdier duality
 on~$X$.
\item \emph{Chiral Hochschild cochains}
 $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA)$ form the cochain-level
 closed-sector endocentral object acting on~$\cA$ in the local
 chiral Swiss-cheese category
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-deligne-tamarkin}). The brace dg algebra
 structure makes $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}$ the universal local
 closed algebra over $\cA$ in the curve-level chiral Swiss-cheese
 sense. A physical factorisation algebra~$T$ enters only through
 a typed brace dg comparison
 $\beta_T\colon \operatorname{Loc}_{\partial}
 \operatorname{Obs}^{\mathrm{bulk}}(T)
 \to C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA)$, and it is identified with the
 derived chiral centre only when $\beta_T$ is a quasi-isomorphism
 (Proposition~\ref{prop:thqg-universal-action-not-reconstruction}).
 The complex itself is
 $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA):=
 C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA,\cA)$; its cohomology is
 $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA,\cA)$, and the ordinary chiral centre is only
 $Z_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)=\ChirHoch^0(\cA,\cA)$
 (Definition~\ref{def:thqg-chiral-derived-center}).
\end{enumerate}
The open/closed MC element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$
(\S\ref{sec:thqg-open-closed-realization}) packages both:
its closed projection is the bar-intrinsic $\Theta_\cA$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}), and its mixed projection
is the closed-sector action on the boundary through
$C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA, \cA)$. The shadow obstruction tower
$(\kappa, \mathfrak{C}, \mathfrak{Q}, \ldots)$ lives in the closed
sector; the annulus trace
$\int_{S^1} \mathcal{M}
\simeq \mathrm{HH}_{\bullet,\mathrm{cat}}(\mathcal{M})$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}) is the first modular shadow
of the open sector.

\section{Deformations of a chiral algebra}

Let $\mathcal{A}$ be a chiral algebra on a smooth projective curve~$X$,
with chiral product
$\mu\colon j_*j^*(\mathcal{A}\boxtimes\mathcal{A})\to\Delta_*\mathcal{A}$
(Chapter~\ref{ch:algebraic-foundations}).
\index{obstruction theory|textbf}
A \emph{first-order deformation} of~$\mathcal{A}$ is a
$\mathcal{D}_X$-module
$\mathcal{A}_\epsilon = \mathcal{A}\oplus\epsilon\,\mathcal{A}$
over $k[\epsilon]/(\epsilon^2)$, equipped with a chiral product
$\mu_\epsilon = \mu + \epsilon\,\phi$, where
$\phi\colon j_*j^*(\mathcal{A}\boxtimes\mathcal{A})\to\Delta_*\mathcal{A}$
is a $\mathcal{D}_X$-bimodule map.

The deformed product $\mu_\epsilon$ must satisfy the Borcherds
identity~\cite{Bor92,BD04}:
for sections $a,b,c$ of~$\mathcal{A}$ at pairwise distinct points
$z_1,z_2,z_3\in X$,
\[
\begin{aligned}
 &\operatorname{Res}_{z_1\!=z_2}\!\mu_\epsilon(a(z_1),\mu_\epsilon(b(z_2),c(z_3)))
 - \operatorname{Res}_{z_1\!=z_2}\!\mu_\epsilon(b(z_2),\mu_\epsilon(a(z_1),c(z_3)))\\
 &\qquad= \operatorname{Res}_{z_2\!=z_3}\!\mu_\epsilon(\mu_\epsilon(a(z_1),b(z_2)),c(z_3)).
\end{aligned}
\]
Expanding modulo~$\epsilon^2$ and using the Borcherds identity for~$\mu$,
the $\epsilon$-coefficient gives:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:deformation-cocycle}
\begin{split}
 \operatorname{Res}_{z_1\!=z_2}\!\bigl[\phi(a,\mu(b,c))
 &+ \mu(a,\phi(b,c))\\
 &- \phi(b,\mu(a,c))
 - \mu(b,\phi(a,c))\bigr]\\
 &= \operatorname{Res}_{z_2\!=z_3}\!\bigl[\phi(\mu(a,b),c)
 + \mu(\phi(a,b),c)\bigr].
\end{split}
\end{equation}
This is a cocycle condition: $\phi$ is closed in a complex whose
differential is built from~$\mu$ via the residue operations above.
That complex is the \emph{chiral Hochschild complex}
$C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{chiral}}(\mathcal{A})$, constructed in
\S\ref{subsec:hochschild-duality}.

The cocycle condition~\eqref{eq:deformation-cocycle} involves three
marked points on~$X$ and residues as pairs collide. An $n$-cochain
in the chiral Hochschild complex involves $(n+2)$ points on~$X$;
the differential acts by residues along the collision divisors
$D_{ij}=\{z_i=z_j\}$ in~$X^{n+2}$. The complex lives on the
configuration space
$C_{n+2}(X)=\{(z_1,\ldots,z_{n+2})\in X^{n+2}: z_i\neq z_j\}$,
and the differential extends to the Fulton--MacPherson
compactification $\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$ as the bar
differential does (Chapter~\ref{chap:bar-cobar}).

At genus $g\geq 1$, the fiberwise differential satisfies
$\dfib^{\,2}=\kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_g$
(Chapter~\ref{ch:heisenberg-frame};
Convention~\ref{conv:higher-genus-differentials}), so the bar complex
is a curved $A_\infty$-algebra. The curvature scalar~$\kappa(\cA)$
obstructs lifting a genus-$0$ deformation to genus~$g$.
Complementarity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}) identifies
$Q_g(\cA)$ and $Q_g(\cA^!)$ as complementary Lagrangians in a
shifted-symplectic space built from
$H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g,\mathcal{Z}(\cA))$. Under the PBW
chiral Koszul, $E_\infty$-completion, and generic/perfectness
hypotheses of Theorem~H, the curve-level chiral Hochschild duality
exchanges deformations and obstructions:
$\ChirHoch^n(\cA)\cong \ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee\otimes\omega_X$
(Remark~\ref{rem:nc-hodge-degeneration}).

\section{The chiral Hochschild cochain complex}

\subsection{The cochain spaces}

A degree-$n$ cochain involves $(n+2)$ marked points on~$X$: one output, $n$ inputs, and one evaluation point.

\begin{definition}[Chiral Hochschild complex, geometric realization]
\label{def:chiral-hochschild-complex}
\index{Hochschild complex!chiral!geometric realization|textbf}
For a chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ on a smooth curve $X$, define the degree $n$ cochains as
\[
C^n_{\text{chiral}}(\mathcal{A}) = \Gamma\left(\overline{C}_{n+2}(X), j_*j^*\mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes (n+2)} \otimes \Omega^n_{\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)}(\log D)\right)
\]
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$ is the Fulton--MacPherson compactification
\item $j: C_{n+2}(X) \to \overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$ is the open embedding
\item $\mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes (n+2)}$ denotes the external tensor product on $X^{n+2}$
\item $\Omega^n_{\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)}(\log D)$ are $n$-forms with logarithmic poles along the boundary divisor $D$
\end{itemize}
This is the \emph{geometric Fulton--MacPherson model} of the chiral
Hochschild complex; the algebraic Ext model
$\Ext^*_{\cA^e}(\cA,\cA)$
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:chirHoch-Ext}} in
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:koszul-pair-structure}}\textup{)} computes
the same chiral derived endomorphism centre under
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:geometric-chiral-hochschild}}; the bigraded
Verdier model is recorded in
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild}} of
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:higher-genus}}. All three
models compute $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ under the
geometric--algebraic comparison hypotheses named in
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-bar-cobar}}. On the PBW chiral
Koszul locus with the $E_{\infty}$-chiral completion hypothesis,
and away from the critical and non-generic quotient loci named in
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}, their common cohomology
has amplitude~$[0,2]$
(Theorem~H, Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}); the
amplitude is the curve-level trace shadow of $K^{2}\simeq\mathrm{id}$
(Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:koszul-reflection}}).
\end{definition}

Explicitly, a degree $n$ cochain is a sum of expressions
\[
\phi = \sum_I a_0^{(I)}(z_0) \otimes a_1^{(I)}(z_1) \otimes \cdots \otimes a_n^{(I)}(z_n) \otimes a_{\infty}^{(I)}(z_{\infty}) \otimes \omega_I
\]
where $a_i^{(I)} \in \mathcal{A}$ and $\omega_I$ is an $n$-form on $\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$ with logarithmic singularities.

\subsection{The differential: three components}

The chiral Hochschild differential
$d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}: C^n_{\text{chiral}} \to C^{n+1}_{\text{chiral}}$
has three components reflecting the algebraic, geometric, and operadic
structures:

\begin{theorem}[The chiral Hochschild differential; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:chiral-hochschild-differential}
The differential decomposes as
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}} = d_{\text{int}} + d_{\text{fact}} + d_{\text{config}}
\]
where:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $d_{\text{int}}$: internal differential from the $\mathcal{D}_X$-module structure
\item $d_{\text{fact}}$: factorization using chiral multiplication
\item $d_{\text{config}}$: de Rham differential on configuration space
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We expand $d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}^{\,2}
= (d_{\text{int}} + d_{\text{fact}}
+ d_{\text{config}})^2$ into six terms (three squares and
three anticommutators) and show that each vanishes on a
generic cochain $\phi \in C^n_{\text{chiral}}$.

\emph{(I) Pure squares.}

\emph{(I.1)} $d_{\text{int}}^2(\phi) = 0$.
The internal differential $d_{\text{int}}$ acts on each
tensor factor $a_i$ by the $\mathcal{D}_X$-module differential
$d_\mathcal{A}$, alternating signs. Since $d_\mathcal{A}^2 = 0$
and the signs follow the standard Koszul rule, this is the
usual chain complex identity.

\emph{(I.2)} $d_{\text{config}}^2(\phi) = 0$.
$d_{\text{config}} = d_{\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)}$ is the
de~Rham differential on the compactified configuration space.
Since $d_{\mathrm{dR}}^2 = 0$, this is immediate.

\emph{(I.3)} $d_{\text{fact}}^2(\phi) = 0$.
Applied to $\phi \in C^n$, $d_{\text{fact}}^2$ composes two
chiral multiplications at distinct pairs of colliding points.
For each pair of collisions $(z_i = z_j)$ and $(z_k = z_l)$
with $\{i,j\} \cap \{k,l\} = \varnothing$, the two residue
extractions commute. For overlapping pairs (sharing a point),
the double residue
$\mathrm{Res}_{z_i = z_j}\mathrm{Res}_{z_j = z_k}$ is the
iterated OPE, which cancels with
$\mathrm{Res}_{z_j = z_k}\mathrm{Res}_{z_i = z_j}$ by
associativity of the chiral product: $\mu \circ (\mu \otimes
\mathrm{id}) = \mu \circ (\mathrm{id} \otimes \mu)$ on the
localizations $j_*j^*$ (the Borcherds identity).

\emph{(II) Mixed anticommutators.}

\emph{(II.1)} $\{d_{\text{int}}, d_{\text{fact}}\}(\phi) = 0$.
The chiral product $\mu\colon j_*j^*(\mathcal{A} \boxtimes
\mathcal{A}) \to \Delta_*\mathcal{A}$ is a morphism of
$\mathcal{D}_X$-modules, so $d_\mathcal{A} \circ \mu =
\mu \circ (d_\mathcal{A} \boxtimes \mathrm{id} +
\mathrm{id} \boxtimes d_\mathcal{A})$. Expanding the
anticommutator term by term, each
$d_\mathcal{A}(\mu(a_i, a_j))$ equals
$\mu(d_\mathcal{A} a_i, a_j) + (-1)^{|a_i|}
\mu(a_i, d_\mathcal{A} a_j)$,
and the signs from $d_{\text{int}}$ and $d_{\text{fact}}$
cancel pairwise.

\emph{(II.2)} $\{d_{\text{int}}, d_{\text{config}}\}(\phi) = 0$.
The logarithmic forms
$\omega \in \Omega^*_{\overline{C}_{n+2}}(\log D)$
are \emph{universal}: they depend only on the configuration
space coordinates $z_i$, not on the algebra data $a_i$.
Therefore $d_\mathcal{A}$ acts only on the $a_i$ factors,
while $d_{\mathrm{dR}}$ acts only on $\omega$. Since the
two differentials act on different tensor factors:
$d_\mathcal{A}(a_i \otimes \omega) =
(d_\mathcal{A} a_i) \otimes \omega$ and
$d_{\mathrm{dR}}(a_i \otimes \omega) =
a_i \otimes d_{\mathrm{dR}}\omega$,
the anticommutator reduces to
$(d_\mathcal{A} \otimes d_{\mathrm{dR}} +
d_{\mathrm{dR}} \otimes d_\mathcal{A})(a_i \otimes \omega)
= 0$ by the Koszul sign rule for the tensor product of
chain complexes.

\emph{(II.3)} $\{d_{\text{fact}}, d_{\text{config}}\}(\phi) = 0$.
The cancellation requires the
Arnold--Orlik--Solomon relations.

On a degree-$1$ cochain
$\phi = a_1 \otimes a_2 \otimes a_3 \otimes
\eta_{12} \in C^1$ (the smallest nontrivial case,
with three points $z_1, z_2, z_3$), the two compositions act
as:
\begin{align*}
(d_{\text{config}} \circ d_{\text{fact}})(\phi)
&= d_{\mathrm{dR}}\Bigl(
 \mathrm{Res}_{z_1 = z_2}\bigl[a_1 a_2 \otimes a_3
 \otimes \eta_{12}\bigr] \Bigr), \\
(d_{\text{fact}} \circ d_{\text{config}})(\phi)
&= \sum_{i<j}
 \mathrm{Res}_{z_i = z_j}\bigl[a_1 \otimes a_2 \otimes a_3
 \otimes d_{\mathrm{dR}}\eta_{12}\bigr].
\end{align*}

The key identity is Arnold's relation
\cite{Arnold69}: for the logarithmic 1-forms
$\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ on $C_3(X)$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:arnold-three-point}
\eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23}
+ \eta_{23} \wedge \eta_{31}
+ \eta_{31} \wedge \eta_{12} = 0.
\end{equation}
Equivalently, $d_{\mathrm{dR}}\eta_{12}$ (which is
supported on the boundary divisor) decomposes as a sum of
residues at $D_{13}$ and $D_{23}$:
\[
d_{\mathrm{dR}}(\eta_{12})
\;\equiv\;
-\eta_{23}\big|_{D_{12}} - \eta_{31}\big|_{D_{12}}
\pmod{\text{smooth forms}}.
\]
In each residue term, $d_{\text{fact}}$ extracts the OPE
at a collision, and $d_{\text{config}}$ produces the
boundary form. The Arnold relation
\eqref{eq:arnold-three-point} ensures these contributions
cancel pairwise, yielding
$\{d_{\text{fact}}, d_{\text{config}}\}(\phi) = 0$.

For general $n$, the argument extends by applying the
generalized Arnold relations on $\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:arnold-relations}): every boundary
stratum of $\overline{C}_{n+2}$ where two points collide
contributes a residue (from $d_{\text{fact}}$) and a
boundary form (from $d_{\text{config}}$), and the
Arnold relations ensure these pair up with opposite signs.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Explicit formula for the differential}

For a cochain $\phi \in C^n_{\text{chiral}}$, the differential acts by:

\begin{align}
(d_{\text{int}}\phi)(&z_0,\ldots,z_{n+1}) = \sum_{i=0}^{n+1} (-1)^i d_{\mathcal{A}}(\phi(z_0,\ldots,\hat{z}_i,\ldots,z_{n+1})) \\
(d_{\text{fact}}\phi)(&z_0,\ldots,z_{n+1}) = \sum_{i=1}^n (-1)^i \text{Res}_{z_i = z_0} \phi(\mu(z_0,z_i),z_1,\ldots,\hat{z}_i,\ldots,z_{n+1}) \\
&+ \sum_{1 \leq i < j \leq n} (-1)^{i+j} \phi(z_0,\ldots,\mu(z_i,z_j),\ldots,\hat{z}_i,\ldots,\hat{z}_j,\ldots,z_{n+1}) \\
(d_{\text{config}}\phi)(&z_0,\ldots,z_{n+1}) = d_{\overline{C}_{n+2}}(\phi)
\end{align}

where $\hat{z}_i$ denotes omission and $\mu$ is the chiral multiplication.

\section{The diagonal bar resolution and the chiral Hochschild spectral sequence}

\subsection{The diagonal bimodule resolution}

\begin{theorem}[chiral Hochschild via bar-cobar; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:hochschild-bar-cobar}
\textup{[Regime: quadratic on the Koszul locus
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

Let $\mathcal{A}$ be a bounded PBW chiral Koszul algebra
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:chiral-koszul-pair})}. The
two-sided chiral bar object
\[
\operatorname{Bar}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(\mathcal{A})
:=
\mathcal{A}\otimes
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})\otimes\mathcal{A}
\]
is a cofibrant replacement of the diagonal
$\mathcal{A}$-$\mathcal{A}$ bimodule. Hence
\[
C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A},\mathcal{A})
\;\simeq\;
R\mathrm{Hom}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(\mathcal{A},\mathcal{A})
\;\simeq\;
\mathrm{Hom}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}
\bigl(\operatorname{Bar}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(\mathcal{A}),\mathcal{A}\bigr).
\]
The algebra quasi-isomorphism
$\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})\simeq
\mathcal{A}$ is the bar--cobar inversion used to build this
resolution. The Koszul dual algebra remains the separate Verdier
object~$\mathcal{A}^{!}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The bar construction $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})$ is a
cofree conilpotent chiral coalgebra. Tensoring it with the left and
right regular $\mathcal{A}$-modules gives the two-sided bar object
$\operatorname{Bar}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(\mathcal{A})$. Its differential
is the sum of the internal differential, the chiral residue
differential, and the two endpoint module actions. The standard
augmentation
\[
\operatorname{Bar}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(\mathcal{A})
\longrightarrow \mathcal{A}
\]
is the diagonal-bimodule version of the bar--cobar counit. On the
PBW Koszul locus the associated graded is the quadratic Koszul
resolution, so the augmentation is a quasi-isomorphism.

Applying $\mathrm{Hom}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(-,\mathcal{A})$ computes
$R\mathrm{Hom}_{\mathcal{A}^{e}}(\mathcal{A},\mathcal{A})$. The
Fulton--MacPherson realization of this Hom complex is precisely
$C^{\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A},\mathcal{A})$: an $n$-cochain
is a diagonal bimodule functional on the $(n+2)$-point two-sided bar
configuration, with the three differential pieces of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-hochschild-differential}. Thus the displayed
quasi-isomorphisms compute the chiral derived centre and keep
$\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})$, $\mathcal{A}^{i}$, and
$\mathcal{A}^{!}$ out of the Hochschild-cochain object.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The chiral Hochschild spectral sequence}

\begin{theorem}[chiral Hochschild spectral sequence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:hochschild-spectral-sequence}
There exists a spectral sequence
\[
E_1^{n,q} = H^q(\overline{C}_{n+2}(X), \mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes (n+2)} \otimes \Omega^n_{\log}) \Rightarrow \ChirHoch^{n+q}(\mathcal{A})
\]
where $n$ is the bar degree (number of internal insertions) and $q$ is the sheaf cohomology degree, which are independent indices.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The chiral Hochschild complex $\ChirHoch^*(\mathcal{A})$ is a double complex with horizontal differential $d_{\mathrm{bar}}$ (the bar differential of Definition~\ref{def:bar-differential-complete}) and vertical differential $d_{\mathrm{sheaf}}$ (sheaf cohomology on configuration spaces). Filter by bar degree: $F^n = \bigoplus_{m \geq n} \ChirHoch^{m,*}$. The resulting spectral sequence has $E_0^{n,q} = \Gamma(\overline{C}_{n+2}(X), \mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes(n+2)} \otimes \Omega^n_{\log})$ with $d_0 = d_{\mathrm{sheaf}}$, so $E_1^{n,q} = H^q(\overline{C}_{n+2}(X), \mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes(n+2)} \otimes \Omega^n_{\log})$. Convergence follows from the bounded-below hypothesis on $\mathcal{A}$ and the finite cohomological dimension of configuration spaces.
\end{proof}

For the cyclic refinement relating chiral Hochschild to cyclic homology via Connes' operator, see Theorem~\ref{thm:HC-spectral-sequence}. For formal chiral algebras (quasi-isomorphic to their cohomology), the spectral sequence above degenerates at $E_1$, giving:
\[
\ChirHoch^k(\mathcal{A}) \cong \bigoplus_{n+q=k} H^q(\overline{C}_{n+2}(X), \mathcal{A}^{\boxtimes (n+2)} \otimes \Omega^n_{\log})
\]

\section{Koszul duality for chiral algebras}

\subsection{Quadratic chiral algebras and their duals}

\begin{definition}[Quadratic chiral algebra]
A chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ is \emph{quadratic} if it admits a presentation
\[
\mathcal{A} = T_{\text{chiral}}(\mathcal{V})/(R)
\]
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\mathcal{V}$ is a locally free $\mathcal{O}_X$-module of generators
\item $T_{\text{chiral}}(\mathcal{V})$ is the free chiral algebra on $\mathcal{V}$
\item $R \subset j_*j^*(\mathcal{V} \boxtimes \mathcal{V})$ consists of quadratic relations
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

The free chiral algebra requires care. Following Beilinson--Drinfeld:

\begin{definition}[Free chiral algebra]
The free chiral algebra on $\mathcal{V}$ is
\[
T_{\text{chiral}}(\mathcal{V}) = \bigoplus_{n \geq 0} \pi_{n*}\left(j_*j^*\mathcal{V}^{\boxtimes n} \otimes \mathcal{D}_{C_n(X)/X}\right)^{\Sigma_n}
\]
where $\pi_n: C_n(X) \to X$ is the projection and $\mathcal{D}_{C_n(X)/X}$ denotes relative differential operators.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Koszul dual]
The Koszul dual of a quadratic chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ is
\[
\mathcal{A}^! = T_{\text{chiral}}(\mathcal{V}^*)/(R^{\perp})
\]
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\mathcal{V}^* = \mathcal{H}om_{\mathcal{O}_X}(\mathcal{V}, \omega_X)$ is the dual shifted by the canonical bundle
\item $R^{\perp}$ consists of relations orthogonal to $R$ under the canonical pairing
\[
\langle \cdot, \cdot \rangle: j_*j^*(\mathcal{V}^* \boxtimes \mathcal{V}) \to j_*\omega_{X^2 \setminus \Delta}
\]
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Three objects]\label{rem:koszul-dual-meaning}
The bar construction $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ is the
bar \emph{coalgebra}: a conilpotent dg coalgebra cogenerated
by~$\mathcal{V}^*$ with corelations~$R^{\perp}$.
Its bar cohomology
\[
\cA^i := H^*\bigl(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr)
\]
is the dual \emph{coalgebra}. The Koszul dual \emph{algebra}
is obtained only after Verdier duality on the curve:
\[
\cA^! := \mathbb{D}_X(\cA^i).
\]
Only on finite-type lanes does this reduce to an ordinary
graded linear dual. The cobar of the bar recovers~$\cA$
itself:
$\Omega(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)) \simeq \cA$
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}\textup{)}.
Thus the corrected comparison chain is
\[
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\cA^i
\;\xrightarrow{\ \mathbb{D}_X\ }\;
\cA^!,
\]
with inversion $\Omega(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)) \simeq \cA$
separate from Koszul duality.
\end{remark}

\begin{example}[Explicit correspondence for Heisenberg]
For the Heisenberg chiral algebra $\mathcal{H}_k$ at level~$k$ with generator $\alpha(z)$ and OPE:
\[\alpha(z)\alpha(w) \sim \frac{k}{(z-w)^2}\]

The Koszul dual $\mathcal{H}^!$ has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Dual generator}: $\alpha^*(z)$ with $\langle \alpha, \alpha^* \rangle = 1$ under residue pairing
\item \emph{Coproduct}:
 \[\Delta(\alpha^*) = \alpha^* \otimes 1 + 1 \otimes \alpha^* + \text{(higher order terms)}\]
 encoding the dual of the commutative algebra structure
\item \emph{Bar construction}: $\bar{B}^{\text{ch}}(\mathcal{H})$ consists of forms like:
 \[\alpha(z_1) \otimes \cdots \otimes \alpha(z_n) \otimes \eta_{12} \wedge \eta_{23} \wedge \cdots\]
 whose residues extract the coproduct coefficients
\end{itemize}

The cobar of the bar recovers $\mathcal{H}$ itself: $\Omega^{\text{ch}}(\bar{B}^{\text{ch}}(\mathcal{H})) \simeq \mathcal{H}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-inversion-qi}).
\end{example}

\begin{remark}[Koszul dual versus dual]
``Koszul dual'' emphasizes the derived character
(bar-cobar construction, quasi-isomorphisms, involutivity:
$(\mathcal{A}^!)^! \simeq \mathcal{A}$). For quadratic $\mathcal{A}$,
this recovers the classical quadratic dual.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The universal twisting morphism}

The universal twisting morphism
$\pi\colon \barB_X(\cA) \to \cA$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:universal-twisting-adjunction}) controls
all bar-cobar identifications in this chapter. Twisting morphisms
are MC elements in the convolution algebra $\mathrm{Hom}(C, A)$
(Definition~\ref{def:twisting-morphism}). The natural bijection
$\mathrm{Tw}(C, A) \cong \mathrm{Hom}(C, B(A)) \cong
\mathrm{Hom}(\Omega(C), A)$
mediates the bar-cobar adjunction
(Proposition~\ref{prop:universal-twisting-adjunction}(iii)); for the
geometric realization as a propagator integral, see
Remark~\ref{rem:twisting-as-propagator}.

\begin{example}[Twisting for fermion-boson duality]
\label{ex:fermion-boson-twisting}
For the Koszul pair (free fermions $\mathcal{F}$, $\beta\gamma$
system), the universal twisting morphism
$\pi\colon \barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{F}) \to \mathcal{F}$
takes the explicit form
$\pi(\psi^*)(z) = \operatorname{Res}_{w=z}\, \psi(w) \cdot \frac{dw}{z-w}$,
implementing the fermion-boson correspondence at the MC level
(Remark~\ref{rem:twisting-as-propagator}).
\end{example}

\subsection{Curve-level chiral Hochschild duality $\ChirHoch^n(\cA)\cong\ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee\otimes\omega_X$}\label{subsec:hochschild-duality}

\begin{lemma}[Fulton--MacPherson collapse and chiral Hochschild duality
shift; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!duality shift computation}
For a chiral Koszul pair $(\cA, \cA^!)$ on a smooth projective
curve~$X$, and for each bar degree~$p$, let
$F_p^\bullet \overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ denote the
Fulton--MacPherson collision-depth filtration by closed unions of
strata of codimension at least the filtration index.
The induced filtration on the bigraded chiral Hochschild complex
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild})}
gives a first-quadrant spectral sequence
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hoch-fm-filtration}
E_1^{r,s}(p)
\;=\;
H^{r+s}\!\Bigl(
\operatorname{gr}_{F_p}^{\,r}
CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\Bigr)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H^{r+s}\!\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr).
\end{equation}
On the Koszul locus this spectral sequence has:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Curve-level $E_2$ page:}
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:hoch-fm-e2}
 E_2^{r,s}(p)=0 \text{ for } s\neq p,
 \qquad
 E_2^{r,p}(p)\cong
 \Ext_{\mathcal{D}_X}^r\!\bigl((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X\bigr).
 \end{equation}
\item \emph{$E_2$-degeneration:} all higher differentials
 $d_m$ with $m\geq 2$ vanish. Equivalently,
 $E_2(p)=E_\infty(p)$.
\item \emph{Uniform shift:} the geometric Verdier shift
 $[p+2]$ from $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ and the totalization shift
 $[-p]$ from
 $RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA) :=
 \operatorname{Tot}(\bigoplus_{p \geq 0}
 CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p])$
 combine to the constant shift~$[2]$.
\item \emph{Amplitude bound:} because $\dim_{\mathbb{C}} X = 1$,
 \[
 \Ext_{\mathcal{D}_X}^r\!\bigl((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X\bigr)=0
 \qquad\text{for } r\notin\{0,1,2\}.
 \]
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Fix~$p$.
The FM compactification $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ is stratified by
collision forests; the closed filtration by collision codimension
induces~\eqref{eq:hoch-fm-filtration}.
Each graded piece is a finite direct sum of external tensor products
of a coherent $\mathcal{D}_X$-module on the base curve with the
logarithmic de~Rham complex of a product of local model fibers
$\FM_m(\mathbb{C})$.
The local complex on the fiber is exactly the bar complex governing
iterated OPE residues at the corresponding collision pattern.

By Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration}, the local bar cohomology is
concentrated in bar-differential degree~$0$.
Writing
\[
\cA^i_p := H^{p,0}\!\bigl(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr),
\]
the associated graded of the collision-depth filtration is therefore
quasi-isomorphic to a complex on the base curve with coefficient
object~$\cA^i_p$.
Applying degreewise Verdier duality on~$X$ gives the
degree-$p$ piece of the Koszul dual algebra,
\[
(\cA^!)_p = \mathbb{D}_X(\cA^i_p),
\]
which yields the $E_2$-page description~\eqref{eq:hoch-fm-e2}.

The higher differentials vanish for either of two standard reasons.
First, the local fibers $\FM_m(\mathbb{C})$ are formal for
$m\geq 2$ by the configuration-space formality package
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:en-formality}}\textup{)},
so after passing to fiber cohomology there is no remaining
chain-level room for $d_m$ with $m\geq 2$.
Equivalent phrasing: the same strata carry pure mixed Hodge
structures, and Deligne strictness forbids a nonzero
weight-changing differential beyond~$E_2$.
Thus $E_2(p)=E_\infty(p)$.

For the shift, Serre--Verdier duality on the smooth proper variety
$\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ contributes $[p+2]$, since
$\dim_{\mathbb{C}}\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)=p+2$.
The totalization of the bigraded chiral Hochschild complex contributes
$[-p]$, so the net shift on every surviving $E_\infty$-term is
$(p+2)-p=2$.
The remaining twist is the base-curve dualizing sheaf~$\omega_X$.

Finally, on a smooth complex curve the global Ext functor for
holonomic $\mathcal{D}_X$-modules has amplitude~$[0,2]$.
Hence the only nonzero columns on the $E_2$-page are
$r=0,1,2$, proving the amplitude statement.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Per-bar-degree to totalization amplitude transport;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{lem:totalization-amplitude}
\index{Hochschild!totalization amplitude}
\textup{[Regime: ordered $E_{1}$-chiral, before averaging;
Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags}}.]}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$. Let
\[
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;=\;
\operatorname{Tot}^{\oplus}\!\Bigl(
\bigoplus_{p \geq 0}
CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]
\Bigr)
\]
be the bigraded chiral Hochschild totalization
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild})}.
Suppose that, after the constant shift~$[2]$ established in
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}}\textup{(iii)},
each bar-degree-$p$ summand
$CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]$ has cohomological
amplitude~$[0, 2]$ as an object of $D^{\mathrm{b}}(\Vect)$,
independently of $p$. Assume also that the computation is made first
in finite conformal-weight/PBW windows, so only finitely many bar
degrees occur in each window, and that the later weight completion is
Mittag--Leffler. Then the direct-sum totalization
$RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$, and its stated completed realization, have
cohomological amplitude~$[0, 2]$; equivalently
$H^n(RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)) = 0$ for $n \notin \{0, 1, 2\}$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The key point is that the totalization is a \emph{direct sum},
not a direct product. By
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild}}, the underlying
bigraded vector space is
\[
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;=\;
\operatorname{Tot}^{\oplus}\!\left(
\bigoplus_{p \geq 0}
\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]\bigr)
\right)
\]
with a total differential
$d_{\mathrm{tot}} = d_{\mathrm{int}} + d_{\mathrm{bar}}$, where
$d_{\mathrm{int}}$ acts within each bar-degree-$p$ summand and
$d_{\mathrm{bar}}$ is the bar-degree-increasing differential
of weight $+1$.

Filter $RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ by bar degree:
$F^p = \bigoplus_{q \geq p} CH^{q,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-q]$.
This is a decreasing filtration. The associated graded is
$\operatorname{gr}_F^{\,p} = CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]$
with the differential induced by $d_{\mathrm{int}}$ alone, since
$d_{\mathrm{bar}}$ strictly increases the bar-degree filtration
and is therefore zero on $\operatorname{gr}_F$.

The induced spectral sequence has
\[
E_1^{p,q}
\;=\;
H^{p+q}\!\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]\bigr)
\;=\;
H^{q+p+(-p)}\!\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H^{p+q}\!\bigl(RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr).
\]
By the per-bar-degree amplitude hypothesis, after the constant
shift~$[2]$ the cohomology
$H^{n}\!\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]\bigr)$
vanishes outside $n \in \{0, 1, 2\}$. Hence
$E_1^{p,q} = 0$ unless $p + q \in \{0, 1, 2\}$, equivalently
$q \in \{-p, 1-p, 2-p\}$.

\smallskip
\emph{Convergence.}\;
Work first in a finite conformal-weight/PBW window. In such a window
the PBW finite-type hypothesis bounds the possible bar lengths, so the
bar-degree filtration is finite, exhaustive
$F^0=RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$, and separated. The spectral sequence
therefore converges strongly in that window. Passing from finite
windows to the direct-sum realization is an exact filtered colimit in
$\Vect$, so no new cohomology appears outside the degrees already
seen in the windows. Passing further to the completed realization is
the separate inverse-limit step; the required
$R^1\!\varprojlim$ term is precisely the Mittag--Leffler defect
$\lambda^1_n(\cA)$ recorded in
Remark~\ref{rem:theorem-H-filter-exactness}, and it vanishes by
hypothesis.

\smallskip
\emph{Amplitude transport.}\;
By the convergence and the $E_1$-page support,
$H^n\!\bigl(RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr)$ vanishes for
$n \notin \{0, 1, 2\}$. The bound $n \geq 0$ uses the
explicit interval $p + q \in \{0, 1, 2\}$ on the $E_1$-page;
the bound $n \leq 2$ likewise.

\smallskip
\emph{No cancellation across bar degrees.}\;
A potential concern is that the bar-degree differential
$d_{\mathrm{bar}}$, which is zero on $\operatorname{gr}_F$
but nonzero on the totalization, is the only possible source of
new cohomology classes outside $\{0, 1, 2\}$ from boundaries
that pair across bar degrees. The spectral sequence
of a filtered complex is precisely the device that tracks all
such pairings: the $E_1$-page records the $d_{\mathrm{int}}$
cohomology, and higher differentials~$d_r$ for $r \geq 1$
record the contributions of $d_{\mathrm{bar}}$ at depth~$r$.
By the Koszul-locus hypothesis and the FM-formality of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}}, every
$d_r$ with $r \geq 2$ vanishes; so the only nontrivial higher
differential is $d_1$, which moves $(p,q) \mapsto (p+1, q)$
and therefore preserves $p + q \mapsto p + q + 1$ -- keeping
the support of the spectral sequence within
$p + q \in \{0, 1, 2, 3\}$. The amplitude bound $p + q \leq 2$
on $E_\infty$ then follows because $d_1$-targets in
$p + q = 3$ that are nontrivial require $E_2$-classes
in $p + q = 3$, but the per-summand vanishing of
$H^{p+q}\!\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)[-p]\bigr)$
for $p + q = 3$ already kills these on the $E_1$-page.
Hence $E_\infty^{p,q} = 0$ for $p + q \notin \{0, 1, 2\}$,
and the totalization has amplitude $[0, 2]$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the bridging lemma is non-trivial]
\label{rem:totalization-amplitude-non-triviality}
A direct sum of complexes each with amplitude $[0, 2]$ has
amplitude $[0, 2]$ \emph{as a graded vector space}, but the
totalization of a bicomplex (with a bar-degree-increasing
$d_{\mathrm{bar}}$ on top of the internal $d_{\mathrm{int}}$)
is \emph{not} just the direct-sum complex: the bar
differential creates cross-bar-degree pairings.
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:totalization-amplitude}} proves
that, on the Koszul locus, no such cross-bar-degree pairing
spreads cohomology outside the $\{0, 1, 2\}$ window. The
control is supplied by the bar-degree filtration spectral
sequence, whose $E_1$-page support is controlled by the
per-bar-degree amplitude bound and whose higher differentials
are killed by FM-formality
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}}\textup{)}.
Without this bridging step, the proof of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}}\textup{(a)}
is incomplete: the sentence ``every column has
amplitude $[0,2]$, hence the totalization does'' becomes true
only after the bar-degree differential is shown not to create
new cohomology classes in degrees outside
$\{0, 1, 2\}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Quadratic-chiral Koszul transfer; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul}
\index{Koszul duality!quadratic chiral transfer|textbf}
\index{Fresse!quadratic operadic Koszul}
Let $\cP$ be a quadratic chiral operad on the smooth curve~$X$
with generators in degree~$2$ and relations in degree~$3$, and
let $\cP^{!}$ denote its chiral operadic Koszul dual
\textup{(}constructed by $\cD_X$-linear duality on the space
of relations, with the chiral pairing induced by OPE residue
at the principal collision\textup{)}. Then there is a
degree-preserving chain map
\[
\sigma \;\colon\; \cP^{!}
\;\longrightarrow\;
T^{c}\!\bigl(s^{-1}\,\overline{\cP}\bigr)^{\vee},
\]
from $\cP^{!}$ into the linear dual of the cofree tensor
coalgebra on the desuspended augmentation ideal
$\overline{\cP} = \ker(\epsilon_\cP)$, intertwining the
operadic Koszul differential on the source with the bar
differential on the target. In equations,
\[
\sigma \circ d_{\mathrm{K}}
\;=\;
d_{\bar{B}}^{\vee} \circ \sigma.
\]
The map $\sigma$ is an isomorphism on the degree-$2$ generator
piece, and its induced map on cohomology is a quasi-isomorphism
whenever $\cP$ is chiral Koszul.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
We transport the quadratic Koszul construction of
Fresse \cite[Ch.~7]{Fresse2017} from the category of dg
symmetric operads over a field to the category of chiral
operads on~$X$ along the OPE-residue pairing. The transport
requires one non-tautological input, recorded in
Step~1 below: the OPE-residue pairing on the weight-$3$ free
operad piece is non-degenerate on the relation space~$R$.
All subsequent steps are formal consequences of Fresse's construction
once non-degeneracy is in hand.

\smallskip
\emph{Step 1 (non-degeneracy of the OPE-residue pairing on
$\cF(E)(3)$).}
We first prove that the chiral pairing
$\langle -,-\rangle_{\mathrm{OPE}}$, obtained by iterated OPE
residues at the principal collision on
$\overline{C}_{3}(X)$, is non-degenerate on the free-operad
degree-$3$ piece $\cF(E)(3)$. The argument is local: by
$\cD_{X^2}$-flatness of~$E$ and the smoothness of~$X$, the
free-operad piece $\cF(E)(3)$ is a locally free
$\cD_{X^3}$-module whose fibre at a generic point $p \in X$
is the classical free-operad piece on the fibre
$E_{p} \in \Vect$. Under this fibrewise identification the
OPE-residue pairing restricts to the classical composition
pairing of Fresse
\cite[Prop.~7.1.3]{Fresse2017}, which is non-degenerate on
$\cF(E_{p})(3)$. Non-degeneracy at a generic point, together
with $\cD_{X^3}$-coherence and semicontinuity of matrix rank,
propagates to all points of the configuration space; where
the pairing specialises (collision divisors), the specialisation
factors through the local model $\FM_{3}(\C)$, on whose real
cohomology the induced pairing descends to the classical
composition pairing on the Arnold algebra
$H^*(\FM_3(\C);\R)$ via the cohomological
$\En$-formality quasi-isomorphism
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:en-formality}}\textup{;}
used here only at the cohomology level, not as a chain-level
$\En$-structure claim\textup{)}, and is non-degenerate on that
Arnold algebra by Fresse
\cite[Prop.~7.1.3]{Fresse2017} applied to the degree-$3$ piece.
Thus $R^{\perp} \subset \cF(E)(3)$ is a well-defined
$\cD_{X^3}$-submodule of complementary rank, and the chiral
Koszul dual $\cP^{!}$ is well defined.

\smallskip
\emph{Step 2 (Fresse transport).}
The quadratic datum is a triple $(E,R,\gamma)$ with
$E \in \operatorname{Mod}(\cD_{X^2})$ the generating
space \textup{(}chiral degree~$2$\textup{)},
$R \subset \cF(E)(3)$ the relation space in free-operad
degree~$3$, and $\gamma$ the structural map. The chiral Koszul
dual has generator space $E^{\vee}[1]$ and relation space
$R^{\perp}$ as constructed in Step~1. Fresse's construction
\cite[Theorem~7.3.1]{Fresse2017} produces, for any
such quadratic datum over a base symmetric-monoidal category,
a canonical chain map
$\sigma_{\mathrm{Fresse}} \colon (P)^{!} \to
B(P)^{\vee}$, where $B$ is the operadic bar
construction. The transfer to the chiral setting replaces
$B$ by the chiral bar $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}$ and the
composition pairing by the OPE-residue pairing of Step~1.
The compatibility of $d_{\mathrm{K}}$ with $d_{\bar{B}}^{\vee}$
then holds because both sides are computed by the same
collision-residue formula
\textup{(}Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}}\textup{)}.

On the degree-$2$ generator piece, $\sigma$ restricts to the
canonical identification $E^{\vee} \cong (s^{-1}\overline{\cP})^{\vee}_1$,
which is a degree-preserving isomorphism by construction.
When $\cP$ is chiral Koszul, the bar cohomology
$H^{*}(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cP))$ is concentrated in
tensor degree~$1$ \textup{(}by the definition of chiral
Koszulness, equivalent
\textup{(}i\textup{)}\textup{)}, and the Fresse transfer
identifies this concentrated cohomology with $\cP^{!}$ via
$\sigma$. Hence $\sigma$ is a quasi-isomorphism whenever
$\cP$ is chiral Koszul, which is the statement of the lemma.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Configuration-space collapse via FM-formality
spectral sequence; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{prop:fm-tower-collapse}
\index{configuration space!collapse|textbf}
\index{Fulton--MacPherson!formality spectral sequence}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$. The bigraded chiral Hochschild complex
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild})}
places degree-$p$ cochains on the Fulton--MacPherson
compactification $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ of complex
dimension~$p+2$. There is a spectral sequence, the
\emph{FM-formality spectral sequence}, that collapses the
entire tower $\{\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)\}_{p \geq 0}$ to the
curve-level $\cD_X$-Ext computation of
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}}.
Precisely:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Filtration by insertion number.}\;
 The FM compactification $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ admits a
 stratification by collision patterns. The maximal
 collision stratum (all $p+2$ points colliding to a single
 point of~$X$) fibers $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ over~$X$ with
 fiber the local model $\FM_{p+2}(\C)$. The collision-depth
 filtration of Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}}
 gives a spectral sequence converging to
 $H^*\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr)$ whose
 $E_0$-page at filtration level~$r$ involves the cohomology
 of configuration spaces $\FM_m(\C)$ for clusters of
 size~$m$.

\item \emph{FM fiber formality and the Arnold algebra.}\;
 By Kontsevich formality
 \textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:en-formality}}\textup{)},
 each local fiber $\FM_m(\C)$ for $m \geq 2$ is formal: its
 real cohomology algebra $H^*(\FM_m(\C); \R)$ is the
 \emph{Arnold algebra}
 \[
 \cAr_m
 \;:=\;
 \bigwedge[\omega_{ij}]_{1 \leq i < j \leq m}
 \Big/
 \bigl(\omega_{ij}\wedge\omega_{jk}
 + \omega_{jk}\wedge\omega_{ki}
 + \omega_{ki}\wedge\omega_{ij}
 \bigr),
 \]
 where $\omega_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ has cohomological
 degree~$1$. This algebra has cohomological amplitude
 $[0, m-1]$: the Poincar\'{e} polynomial is
 $\prod_{j=1}^{m-1}(1+jt)$, with top class in
 degree~$m-1$, and $H^k(\FM_m(\C)) = 0$ for
 $k > m-1$. In particular, $\FM_2(\C)$ has
 amplitude~$[0,1]$.

\item \emph{PBW-Koszulness routes Arnold collapse without
 invoking bar concentration.}\;
 The $d_1$-differential on the collision-depth spectral
 sequence annihilates every Arnold class of positive fibre
 degree by a route that bypasses
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bar-concentration}}. The argument
 uses three independent inputs, each intrinsic to its
 home category: the PBW-Koszulness criterion
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}\textup{)}
 for the chiral operad, the quadratic Koszulness of the
 braid-arrangement Orlik--Solomon algebra
 \cite{SheltonYuzvinsky1997}, and the chiral-quadratic
 transfer of
 Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul}}.

 At bar degree~$p$, the $E_1$-page carries contributions
 from every collision pattern on the $p+2$ colliding points:
 partial collisions on intermediate configuration spaces,
 and the full collision to a single point of~$X$. Each
 pattern contributes through the Arnold-algebra cohomology
 of the corresponding local fibre, coupled by the Arnold
 differential~$d_1$ induced from the chiral OPE residues.
 The PBW hypothesis on~$\cA$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}\textup{)}
 delivers a homogeneous quadratic presentation of the chiral
 endomorphism operad at every local fibre; Shelton--Yuzvinsky
 delivers the contracting homotopy on the Arnold side;
 Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul}} transports
 that homotopy across~$\sigma$ onto the bar side. All
 higher-filtration Arnold classes, which record the topology
 of intermediate collision patterns in $\FM_m(\C)$ for
 $m \geq 3$, are annihilated on the $E_1$-page by this
 transported homotopy.

\item \emph{Surviving contribution.}\;
 The sole surviving $E_2$-term comes from the deepest
 collision stratum, where all $p+2$ points have fully
 collided to a single point of~$X$. After
 bar-concentration, this stratum contributes the coefficient
 $\cD_X$-module $\cA^i_p = H^{p,0}(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA))$
 on the base curve. Applying Verdier duality on~$X$ gives
 $(\cA^!)_p = \mathbb{D}_X(\cA^i_p)$, and the surviving
 $E_2$-terms are
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:fm-tower-surviving}
 E_2^{r,p}(p)
 \;\cong\;
 \Ext_{\cD_X}^r\!\bigl((\cA^!)_p, \omega_X\bigr),
 \qquad
 E_2^{r,s}(p) = 0 \;\text{for}\; s \neq p.
 \end{equation}

\item \emph{Amplitude from the base curve.}\;
 The curve-level Ext on a smooth projective curve satisfies
 \[
 \Ext_{\cD_X}^r\!\bigl(\cM, \omega_X\bigr) = 0
 \qquad\text{for }r \notin \{0,1,2\}
 \]
 for any holonomic $\cD_X$-module~$\cM$.
 Therefore the total cohomological amplitude of
 $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$ is $[0,2]$: the FM tower of
 configuration spaces of unbounded dimension contributes
 \emph{zero} net amplitude beyond the base curve, because
 bar-concentration eliminates all fiber cohomology above
 degree~$0$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The spectral sequence is the collision-depth filtration spectral
sequence of Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation},
repackaged to make the tower collapse explicit.

\emph{Step~1: stratification.}\;
The FM compactification $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ is stratified by
collision forests: rooted trees recording which points collide.
Each stratum is a fiber bundle whose base is a product of
configuration spaces of~$X$ (recording the positions of
collision clusters on the curve) and whose fiber is a product
of local FM spaces $\FM_{m_i}(\C)$ (recording the collision
pattern within each cluster, where $m_i$ is the cluster size).

\emph{Step~2: $E_1$-page from Arnold algebras.}\;
At each stratum, the fiber cohomology is computed by the Arnold
algebra. For a cluster of $m$ points, the Arnold algebra
$\cAr_m$ has cohomological amplitude $[0, m-1]$.
Formality (Proposition~\ref{prop:en-formality}) ensures that the
fiber cohomology is computed entirely by $\cAr_m$; there are no
higher chain-level corrections. The $E_1$-page of the
collision-depth spectral sequence is thus a complex whose terms
involve the Arnold algebras of all cluster sizes occurring in
the collision forest, tensored with the $\cD_X$-module
coefficient system from the base.

\emph{Step~3: Arnold-algebra Koszulness gives a contracting
homotopy on the $E_1$-page.}\;
We show that the $d_1$-differential on the collision-depth
spectral sequence kills all $E_1$-classes coming from the
Arnold-algebra cohomology in degrees $k \geq 1$, without
invoking Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration}. The argument
is intrinsic to the Arnold algebra and the chiral operadic
Koszul dual, and proceeds through three inputs.

\emph{\textup{(3a)} Arnold algebra is quadratic Koszul.}\;
The Arnold algebra $\cAr_m$ is the Orlik--Solomon algebra of
the type-$A_{m-1}$ braid arrangement, presented by
quadratic relations (the Arnold three-term relation on each
pair of overlapping indices). By the Shelton--Yuzvinsky
theorem \cite{SheltonYuzvinsky1997}, every
supersolvable hyperplane arrangement yields a quadratic Koszul
Orlik--Solomon algebra; the $A_{m-1}$ arrangement is
supersolvable, so $\cAr_m$ is quadratic Koszul. Concretely,
this provides a canonical minimal free resolution of the
ground ring over $\cAr_m$ which is linear (generators in a
single internal degree at each homological step) and, dually,
a contracting homotopy
\[
h_m \;\colon\; {\cAr_m}^{\geq 1} \longrightarrow {\cAr_m}^{\geq 1}
\]
of the augmented Arnold complex onto the ground field,
satisfying $d h_m + h_m d = \id - \pi_0$, where $\pi_0$ is
projection onto $H^{0}(\FM_m(\C)) = \R$. The map $h_m$ is
canonical (determined by the supersolvable flag) and acts
fibrewise on the $E_1$-page of the collision-depth spectral
sequence.

\emph{\textup{(3b)} Chiral-quadratic transfer to the bar
coalgebra.}\;
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul} provides a chain map
$\sigma \colon \cP^{!} \to T^{c}(s^{-1}\overline{\cP})^{\vee}$
for every quadratic chiral operad~$\cP$, intertwining the
Koszul differential with the bar differential. Taking $\cP$
to be the degree-$(\leq m)$ truncation of the chiral
endomorphism operad $\End^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\cA}$ at the local
fiber $\FM_m(\C)$ \textup{(}which is quadratic because $\cA$ is
chiral Koszul\textup{)}, $\sigma$ identifies the Arnold-algebra
cohomology on the fiber with the linear dual of the bar
complex on that fiber. The composition
$\sigma \circ h_m \circ \sigma^{-1}$ is then a contracting
homotopy for the bar differential on the fiber, in degrees
$\geq 1$.

\emph{\textup{(3c)} Fibrewise killing of higher Arnold
classes.}\;
Consider a stratum indexed by a collision pattern with cluster
sizes $(m_1, \ldots, m_\ell)$, $\sum m_i = p+2$. The fiber at
this stratum is $\prod_{i=1}^{\ell} \FM_{m_i}(\C)$, with
Arnold cohomology in degrees
$[0, \sum_i (m_i - 1)] = [0, p+2-\ell]$. The tensor product
$h = h_{m_1} \otimes \cdots \otimes h_{m_\ell}$ is, by the
Koszul property of each factor, a contracting homotopy for
the Arnold differential on the product stratum in fibre
degrees~$\geq 1$. Transporting $h$ through $\sigma$ yields a
contracting homotopy for the $d_1$-differential on the
$E_1$-page of the collision-depth spectral sequence, fibrewise
over the base configuration of cluster locations. Hence
$E_2$-classes supported on fibre degree~$\geq 1$ vanish.

The sole surviving $E_2$-contribution at each filtration
level is the fibre-degree-$0$ class, which is
$H^0(\FM_m(\C)) = \R$ independently of~$m$. For
$\ell < p+2$, this collapses the partial-collision stratum
to its base, which itself lies in lower filtration degree;
iterating, only the full-collision $\ell = 1$, $m_1 = p+2$
survives. This completes Step~3 without any appeal to
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration}: the tower collapse is
powered by the quadratic Koszulness of the Arnold algebra
and the chiral-operadic transfer of
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul}.

\emph{Step~4: the survivor is the full-collision stratum.}\;
The unique surviving stratum is the full-collision
$\ell = 1$, $m_1 = p + 2$: all points collide to a single
location on~$X$. This stratum fibers over~$X$ with fiber
$\FM_{p+2}(\C)$. The transported homotopy of Step~3 forces
the fibre contribution to the degree-$0$ piece of the Arnold
algebra $\cAr_{p+2}$, which is
$H^0(\FM_{p+2}(\C)) = \R$ (a point). The coefficient system
on the base~$X$ is the $\cD_X$-module
$\cA^i_p = H^{p,0}(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA))$,
the degree-$p$ bar cohomology.

\emph{Step~5: Verdier duality and curve-level Ext.}\;
Applying degreewise Verdier duality on~$X$ replaces the
bar cohomology coalgebra $\cA^i_p$ with the Koszul dual
algebra piece $(\cA^!)_p = \mathbb{D}_X(\cA^i_p)$.
The surviving $E_2$-terms are therefore
$\Ext_{\cD_X}^r((\cA^!)_p, \omega_X)$ for $r = 0, 1, 2$,
which is~\eqref{eq:fm-tower-surviving}.

\emph{Step~6: the shift arithmetic.}\;
The net degree shift is $(p + 2) - p = 2$: the Verdier shift
$[p+2]$ from $\dim_{\C} \overline{C}_{p+2}(X) = p + 2$
minus the totalization shift~$[-p]$ from the bigraded complex
(Definition~\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild}). This constant
shift~$[2]$, independent of~$p$, is the origin of the uniform
duality $\ChirHoch^n(\cA) \cong
\ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^{\vee} \otimes \omega_X$.

\emph{Step~7: degeneration at $E_2$.}\;
Higher differentials $d_m$ for $m \geq 2$ vanish by FM-formality.
The local fibers carry pure mixed Hodge structures
(Proposition~\ref{prop:en-formality}), and Deligne strictness
forbids weight-changing differentials beyond~$E_2$.
Therefore $E_2 = E_\infty$.

The proposition follows: the full tower
$\{\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)\}_{p \geq 0}$ of configuration spaces
of unbounded dimension collapses, via the FM-formality
spectral sequence, to the curve-level
$\cD_X$-Ext computation of
Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[PBW as common source of two collapses]
\label{rem:pbw-parallel-consequences}
\index{PBW!parallel consequences}
The route to Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}
passes through
Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul}, not through
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration}. PBW is the common
homological source of two parallel consequences,
\[
 \text{PBW collapse}
 \quad\Longrightarrow\quad
 \begin{cases}
 \text{bar concentration}
 & \textup{(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration})}, \\[2pt]
 \text{FM-tower collapse}
 & \textup{(Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse})}.
 \end{cases}
\]
The two conclusions are PBW-parallel: neither invokes the
other after the PBW input has been established. This
structure mirrors the split in the Russian school between
the combinatorial Poincar\'e--Birkhoff--Witt normal form and
the homological concentration of the bar complex: a single
growth hypothesis on the filtration, proved once, has
independent force on both tracks.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Sharp bigraded Hilbert series of
chiral Hochschild; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{prop:chirhoch-sharp-hilbert}
\index{chiral Hochschild!bigraded Hilbert series}
\index{Russian school!sharp Hilbert series}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral Koszul algebra on~$X$ satisfying the
PBW criterion of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}, with
Koszul dual~$\cA^{!}$ and chiral centre $Z(\cA) =
\ChirHoch^{0}(\cA)$. Assume the finite-type/perfectness
hypotheses of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}, so each
$q$-graded coefficient below is finite. The bigraded
Hilbert series
\[
 P_{\cA}(t,q)
 \;=\;
 \sum_{n \geq 0}
 \dim_q \ChirHoch^{n}(\cA)\,t^{n}
\]
is rigidly determined in cohomological degrees $\{0,1,2\}$ by
the Hilbert series of the centre, of the first Hochschild
group, and of the dual centre:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-sharp-hilbert}
 P_{\cA}(t,q)
 \;=\;
 \HS_{Z(\cA)}(q)
 \;+\;
 \HS_{\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)}(q)\cdot t
 \;+\;
 \HS_{Z(\cA^{!})}(q)\cdot t^{2}.
\end{equation}
In particular, $P_{\cA}(t,q)$ is a polynomial of $t$-degree~$2$
with positive $q$-coefficients, and the $t^{0}$- and $t^{2}$-
columns are exchanged by Verdier duality on~$X$; the $t^2$ column
is the Hilbert series of $Z(\cA^!)^\vee\otimes\omega_X$, hence has
the same finite coefficients as $Z(\cA^!)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}, the chiral
Hochschild complex has cohomological amplitude $[0,2]$, so
$\ChirHoch^{n}(\cA)=0$ for $n \notin \{0,1,2\}$ and the sum
terminates at $t^{2}$. The $n=0$ column is the chiral
centre $Z(\cA)=\ChirHoch^{0}(\cA)$ by definition; its
graded dimension furnishes the $t^{0}$-coefficient of
\eqref{eq:chirhoch-sharp-hilbert}. The $n=1$ column is
$\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$ directly; its graded dimension is the
$t^{1}$-coefficient. For $n=2$, the shift arithmetic of
Step~6 in the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}, combined with
degreewise Verdier duality on the base curve
(equation~\eqref{eq:fm-tower-surviving}), identifies
$\ChirHoch^{2}(\cA)$ with the Verdier-dual chiral centre of the
Koszul dual:
$\ChirHoch^{2}(\cA)\cong Z(\cA^{!})^\vee\otimes\omega_X$. The
dualizing twist changes the line-valued realization, not the
finite Hilbert coefficients. Assembling the three
columns yields~\eqref{eq:chirhoch-sharp-hilbert}. The
positivity of the $q$-coefficients follows because each
column is a $\cD_X$-Ext space with values in an ordinary
holonomic $\cD_X$-module, whose fibrewise dimensions
are non-negative integers.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Heisenberg chiral Hochschild concentration;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{cor:chirhoch-heisenberg}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!Heisenberg}
For the Heisenberg chiral algebra $\mathfrak{H}_k$ at generic level,
\[
 \bigl(\dim\ChirHoch^{0},\dim\ChirHoch^{1},\dim\ChirHoch^{2}\bigr)
 \;=\;(1,1,1),
 \qquad
 \dim_{\mathrm{tot}}\ChirHoch^{\bullet}(\mathfrak{H}_k) = 3.
\]
The $t^{0}$- and $t^{2}$-columns are the scalar centre $Z(\mathfrak{H}_k)$
and its Koszul dual $Z(\mathfrak{H}_k^{!}) = Z(\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^{*}))$;
the $t^{1}$-column is the single outer derivation encoding the
level deformation $k \mapsto k + \varepsilon$, the unique chiral
derivation not absorbed by the double-pole OPE.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The abelian zero mode of $\mathfrak{H}_k$ is central, so every
linear derivation on the Heisenberg generator survives the chiral
inner-derivation quotient; by the no-simple-pole dichotomy there
is exactly one. Applying \eqref{eq:chirhoch-sharp-hilbert} with
$Z(\mathfrak{H}_k)=\C$ and $Z(\mathfrak{H}_k^{!})=\C$ recovers the
Hilbert triple.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Affine $\mathfrak{sl}_{2}$ Hochschild total
dimension; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{cor:chirhoch-affine-sl2}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!affine sl_2}
For $V_{k}(\mathfrak{sl}_{2})$ at generic non-critical level,
\[
 \bigl(\dim\ChirHoch^{0},\dim\ChirHoch^{1},\dim\ChirHoch^{2}\bigr)
 \;=\;(1,3,1),
 \qquad
 \dim_{\mathrm{tot}}\ChirHoch^{\bullet}\bigl(V_{k}(\mathfrak{sl}_{2})\bigr) = 5.
\]
The $t^{1}$-column is $\mathfrak{sl}_{2}$ via
Proposition~\ref{prop:chirhoch1-affine-km}; the $t^{0}$ and $t^{2}$
columns are scalar via
Proposition~\ref{prop:derived-center-explicit}(ii) and the Koszul
duality $\dim\ChirHoch^{2} = \dim Z(V_{k'}(\mathfrak{sl}_{2}))$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The Whitehead lemma furnishes $H^{1}(\mathfrak{sl}_{2},\mathfrak{sl}_{2})=0$
at the chiral-commutator level, while the chiral Koszul resolution
with generating space $V=\mathfrak{sl}_{2}$ gives
$\mathrm{Ext}^{1}_{V_{k}(\mathfrak{sl}_{2})}(\C,\C) = \mathfrak{sl}_{2}$
as the space of current deformations $J^{a}\mapsto J^{a} + \varepsilon\phi^{a}$.
K\"unneth over the factorisation base assembles the three columns
$(1,3,1)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Virasoro Hochschild Hilbert series;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{cor:chirhoch-virasoro-hilbert}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!Virasoro Hilbert series}
For the Virasoro algebra $\mathrm{Vir}_{c}$ at generic central
charge,
\[
 P_{\mathrm{Vir}_{c}}(t,q)
 \;=\;
 \HS_{Z(\mathrm{Vir}_{c})}(q)
 \;+\;
 \HS_{\ChirHoch^{1}(\mathrm{Vir}_{c})}(q)\cdot t
 \;+\;
 \HS_{Z(\mathrm{Vir}_{c}^{!})}(q)\cdot t^{2},
\]
with $\HS_{\ChirHoch^{1}(\mathrm{Vir}_{c})}(q) = 0$ at generic~$c$;
the $t^{0}$- and $t^{2}$-columns are scalar and exchanged by the
Feigin--Fuchs involution $c \leftrightarrow 26-c$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The quartic OPE pole of $T(z)T(w)$ forces every chiral derivation
of $\mathrm{Vir}_{c}$ to be inner at generic~$c$, so the Feigin--Fuchs
resolution of $\mathrm{Vir}_{c}$-modules by Fock modules computes
$\ChirHoch^{1}(\mathrm{Vir}_{c}) = 0$ directly, bypassing the bar
complex. The Koszul dual centre is scalar by
Proposition~\ref{prop:derived-center-explicit}; the involution
$c \leftrightarrow 26-c$ is the shadow of the Koszul Reflection
$K^{2}\simeq\id$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Chiral transport of Shelton--Yuzvinsky contracting
homotopy; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{lem:chiral-homotopy-transport}
\index{Shelton--Yuzvinsky!chiral transport}
\index{contracting homotopy!ordered chiral bar}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral Koszul algebra on~$X$ satisfying the
PBW criterion of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}, and fix
$m \geq 2$. Write
$h_m \colon \operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})^{\geq 1}
\to \operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})^{\geq 1}$
for the Shelton--Yuzvinsky contracting homotopy on the
pure-braid Orlik--Solomon algebra of the type-$A_{m-1}$
arrangement \textup{(}the canonical homotopy furnished by the
supersolvable flag on~$A_{m-1}$, satisfying
$d h_m + h_m d = \id - \pi_{0}$, where $\pi_{0}$
projects onto $H^{0}(\FM_m(\C))$\textup{)}. Let
$\sigma$ be the Fresse chain map of
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul}}, applied to the
degree-$(\leq m)$ truncation of the chiral endomorphism operad
$\End^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\cA}$ at the local fibre~$\FM_m(\C)$.
In the Koszul local fibre model
\[
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\bullet}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)}
 \;\simeq\;
 \operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})\otimes\cA^{\otimes m},
\]
represent $\sigma$ by this chain isomorphism. Then the transported
homotopy
\[
 h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}
 \;:=\;
 \sigma \circ (h_m\otimes\id_{\cA^{\otimes m}}) \circ \sigma^{-1}
 \;\colon\;
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)}
 \;\longrightarrow\;
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)}
\]
is a well-defined chain-level contracting homotopy for the
ordered chiral bar differential on that Koszul fibre model, satisfying
\[
 d_{\bar B}\, h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}
 \;+\;
 h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}\, d_{\bar B}
 \;=\;
 \id - \pi_{0}^{\mathrm{ord}}
 \qquad \text{on} \;
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)},
\]
where $\pi_{0}^{\mathrm{ord}}$ is projection onto the degree-$0$
fibre component. The homotopy $h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}$ is
$\Sigma_m$-equivariant in the following sense: the averaging map
$\mathrm{av}\colon \barB^{\mathrm{ord}} \to \barB^{\Sigma}$
intertwines $h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}$ with the induced symmetric-side
contracting homotopy descended from~$h_m$ through the
$\Sigma_m$-invariance of the supersolvable flag.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The Orlik--Solomon algebra $\operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})$ is the
graded-commutative algebra generated by the Arnold forms
$\omega_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ modulo the Arnold three-term
relation, and coincides with
$H^{*}(\FM_m(\C); \R)$ \cite{Arnold1969,OrlikSolomon1980}.
The type-$A_{m-1}$ arrangement is supersolvable (the chain of
subarrangements obtained by successively removing one coordinate
is a modular flag), so by Shelton--Yuzvinsky
\cite{SheltonYuzvinsky1997} the Orlik--Solomon algebra
$\operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})$ is quadratic Koszul. The Koszul
property equips the augmented complex
$(\operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})^{\geq 1}, d)$ with a canonical
contracting homotopy~$h_m$ onto the ground field
\textup{(}the Priddy--Koszul homotopy determined by the
supersolvable flag; see
\cite[Theorem~7.3.1]{Fresse2017}\textup{)}, satisfying
$d h_m + h_m d = \id - \pi_{0}$.

By Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul} the Fresse chain map
$\sigma \colon \cP^{!} \to T^{c}(s^{-1}\overline{\cP})^{\vee}$ is
a quasi-isomorphism whenever $\cP$ is chiral Koszul, with
$\sigma \circ d_{\mathrm{K}} = d_{\bar B}^{\vee} \circ \sigma$.
Taking $\cP$ to be the degree-$(\leq m)$ truncation of the chiral
endomorphism operad $\End^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\cA}$ at the fibre
$\FM_m(\C)$, the PBW hypothesis
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}\textup{)}
supplies a homogeneous quadratic presentation. Passing to the
Koszul local fibre model,~$\sigma$ is represented by a fibrewise
chain isomorphism. Under the identification
\[
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\bullet}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)}
 \;\simeq\;
 \operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1}) \otimes \cA^{\otimes m}
\]
on the Koszul locus (which is the content of the quadratic
Koszul transfer: the ordered chiral bar on the local fibre
tensor-decomposes into the Arnold cohomology of the fibre
coupled with $m$ copies of the algebra), the transported homotopy
$h_m^{\mathrm{ord}} :=
\sigma \circ (h_m\otimes\id_{\cA^{\otimes m}})\circ\sigma^{-1}$
acts as $h_m \otimes \id_{\cA^{\otimes m}}$ on the tensor
decomposition. A direct computation gives
\begin{align*}
 d_{\bar B}\, h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}
 + h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}\, d_{\bar B}
 &= \sigma \circ
 \bigl((d\, h_m + h_m\, d)\otimes\id_{\cA^{\otimes m}}\bigr)
 \circ \sigma^{-1}
 \\
 &= \sigma \circ
 \bigl((\id - \pi_{0})\otimes\id_{\cA^{\otimes m}}\bigr)
 \circ \sigma^{-1}
 \\
 &= \id - \pi_{0}^{\mathrm{ord}},
\end{align*}
using the intertwining
$\sigma \circ d = d_{\bar B}^{\vee} \circ \sigma$ from
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul} and the fact that
$\sigma$ is the identity on the degree-$0$ piece
\textup{(}so $\sigma \circ \pi_0 \circ \sigma^{-1} =
\pi_0^{\mathrm{ord}}$\textup{)}.

For $\Sigma_m$-equivariance: choose the ordered Priddy--Koszul
homotopy $h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}$ and replace it, in characteristic zero,
by the Reynolds average
\[
h_m^\Sigma := \frac{1}{m!}\sum_{\sigma\in\Sigma_m}
\sigma h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}\sigma^{-1}.
\]
This averaged homotopy commutes with the $\Sigma_m$-action and
descends through
$\mathrm{av}\colon \barB^{\mathrm{ord}} \to \barB^{\Sigma}$ to the
Priddy--Koszul homotopy on
$\operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})^{\Sigma_m}$. The diagram
\[
\begin{array}{ccc}
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)}
 & \xrightarrow{\,h_m^{\mathrm{ord}}\,} &
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)} \\[3pt]
 \big\downarrow \mathrm{av} & & \big\downarrow \mathrm{av}
 \\[3pt]
 \barB^{\Sigma}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)/\Sigma_m}
 & \xrightarrow{\,h_m^{\Sigma}\,} &
 \barB^{\Sigma}_{\,\geq 1}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)/\Sigma_m}
\end{array}
\]
commutes, which is the intertwining statement of the lemma.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Chain-level versus cohomology-level scope of the
transported homotopy]
\label{rem:sigma-inverse-chain-level}
The Fresse chain map $\sigma$ of
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul} is only a
quasi-isomorphism in general, so a strict chain-level inverse
$\sigma^{-1}$ need not exist on the ambient complex. The
well-definedness of
$h_m^{\mathrm{ord}} :=
\sigma\circ(h_m\otimes\id_{\cA^{\otimes m}})\circ\sigma^{-1}$
in Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-homotopy-transport} rests on
the stronger identification
\[
 \barB^{\mathrm{ord}}_{\,\bullet}(\cA)\big|_{\FM_m(\C)}
 \;\simeq\;
 \operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1}) \otimes \cA^{\otimes m}
\]
valid on the Koszul locus, in which $\sigma$ restricts to a
chain-level isomorphism of the tensor-decomposed local fibre model.
What Theorem~H consumes is the weaker cohomology-level
statement: the $d_{1}$-differential of the collision-depth
spectral sequence annihilates the positive-degree Arnold classes
on the $E_{1}$-page. This cohomology-level vanishing is the output
of Shelton--Yuzvinsky Koszulness applied fibrewise, and is
insensitive to the chain-level versus cohomology-level distinction
because the spectral-sequence formulation absorbs the
homotopy inverse implicit in any quasi-isomorphic transport.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Ordered-bar chiral Hochschild concentration via
ordered FM and pure braid Orlik--Solomon;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:hochschild-concentration-E1}
\index{Hochschild!ordered-bar concentration}
\index{Orlik--Solomon!pure braid Koszulness}
\textup{[Regime: ordered $E_{1}$-chiral side, before averaging.]}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$ satisfying the PBW criterion of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}.
Write $\ChirHoch^{\mathrm{ord},n}(\cA)$ for the ordered
chiral Hochschild groups computed on
$\overline{C}^{\mathrm{ord}}_{p+2}(X)$ without
$\Sigma_{n}$-coinvariants. Then
\[
 \ChirHoch^{\mathrm{ord},n}(\cA) \;=\; 0
 \qquad
 \textup{for every } n \notin \{0,1,2\},
\]
and this ordered concentration is established on the first
page of the collision-depth spectral sequence on
$\overline{C}^{\mathrm{ord}}_{p+2}(X)$ via pure-braid
Orlik--Solomon Koszulness, without invoking
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bar-concentration}}. The symmetric
statement $\ChirHoch^{n}(\cA)=0$ for $n\notin\{0,1,2\}$ is
obtained by the averaging step of
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We replay the collision-depth spectral sequence on the
ordered FM compactification. Each stratum is a fibre
bundle whose fibre is now a product of ordered local FM
spaces $\FM^{\mathrm{ord}}_{m_i}(\C)$, whose cohomology is
the \emph{pure} braid Orlik--Solomon algebra
$\operatorname{OS}(A_{m_i-1})$ (no $\Sigma_{m_i}$-coinvariants
at any stage; the ordering on $\R$ is kept throughout, in
the ordered E$_1$ chiral structure). The pure braid
arrangement $A_{m-1}$ is supersolvable, hence by
Shelton--Yuzvinsky \cite{SheltonYuzvinsky1997} its
Orlik--Solomon algebra is quadratic Koszul with linear minimal
free resolution and, dually, a canonical contracting
homotopy $h_m$ of
$\operatorname{OS}(A_{m-1})^{\geq 1}$ onto the ground field.
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-homotopy-transport} transports
$h_m$ through the Fresse map~$\sigma$ of
Lemma~\ref{lem:chiral-quadratic-koszul} onto the Koszul local
fibre model of the ordered chiral bar side, producing the
fibrewise contracting homotopy
$h_m^{\mathrm{ord}} =
\sigma\circ(h_m\otimes\id_{\cA^{\otimes m}})\circ\sigma^{-1}$
on the $E_{1}$-page in ordered fibre degrees $\geq 1$, with
no appeal to Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration} and no
$\Sigma_{n}$-averaging step. As in Steps~4--6 of the proof
of Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}, only the
full-collision stratum survives, contributing the
$\cD_X$-Ext amplitude $[0,2]$ on the base curve. Hence
$\ChirHoch^{\mathrm{ord},n}(\cA)=0$ for $n\notin\{0,1,2\}$,
established intrinsically on the ordered $E_{1}$ side.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Derivation-type breakdown across the standard
landscape; \ClaimStatusComputed]
\label{rem:chirhoch-derivation-types}
\index{Hochschild!derivation-type breakdown}
The dimension $\dim\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$ alone is a coarse coordinate.
The chiral Hochschild engine
\textup{(}\texttt{compute/lib/chiral\_hochschild\_engine.py}\textup{)}
records a finer datum: which type of first-order chiral
deformation each derivation realises. The breakdown across the
standard landscape exhibits a structural distinction between
class~$\mathsf G$ \emph{level-deformable} families and class~$\mathsf
L$ \emph{level-rigid} families.
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l c l@{}}
\toprule
Family & $\dim\ChirHoch^{1}$ & Derivation type \\
\midrule
Heisenberg $\cH_k$
 & $1$
 & level deformation $k\mapsto k+\epsilon$ \\
free fermion $\psi$
 & $1$
 & antisymmetric bilinear rescaling \\
$\beta\gamma_\lambda$
 & $2$
 & charge rescaling $\oplus$ weight deformation
   $\lambda\mapsto\lambda+\epsilon$ \\
$V_k(\fg)$ generic
 & $\dim\fg$
 & adjoint-action derivations of $\fg$
   \emph{(}level rigid: $0$-dim\emph{)} \\
$\Vir_c$ generic
 & $0$
 & rigid \emph{(}no first-order chiral deformations\emph{)} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Three observations follow.
\textit{(i) The level rigidity of $V_k(\fg)$.} The chiral Hochschild
engine reports $\dim\ChirHoch^{1}(V_k(\fg)) = \dim\fg$ realised by
\emph{adjoint} derivations of $\fg$, not by level deformations of
$k$. The engine entry is
$\{\mathrm{current\_algebra\_derivations}: \dim\fg,\;
\mathrm{level\_deformation}: 0\}$. The level $k$ is therefore
\textbf{not} a chiral-bimodule deformation of $V_k(\fg)$:
$V_{k+\epsilon}(\fg)$ is structurally a different algebra (different
central extension of $\widehat\fg$), not a deformation in the sense
of $\Hoch^{1}$. Compare this with class $\mathsf G$: for $\cH_k$ the
level $k$ \textbf{is} a chiral-bimodule deformation, because the
abelian OPE $J(z)J(w)\sim k(z-w)^{-2}$ rescales freely. The
asymmetry between class $\mathsf G$ and class $\mathsf L$ in
deformation theory is invisible in the scalar
$\kappa$-stratification but visible at level~$3$ of the open
Beilinson tower.
\textit{(ii) The chiral rigidity of $\Vir_c$.} The Virasoro algebra
at generic central charge $c$ has $\dim\ChirHoch^{1}(\Vir_c) = 0$:
no first-order chiral deformations exist. Within the fixed-$c$
slice, $\Vir_c$ is \textbf{rigid}. The continuous parameter $c$ moves
between distinct fixed-$c$ slices but is external to the
chiral-bimodule deformation theory of any individual $\Vir_c$. The
same holds for $\cW_3$ at generic $c$: $\dim\ChirHoch^{1}(\cW_3)=0$.
This is class~$\mathsf M$ chiral rigidity at generic central charge.
\textit{(iii) The two-derivation structure of $\beta\gamma_\lambda$.}
Class $\mathsf C$ records two distinct deformation directions: a
\emph{charge rescaling} \textup{(}rescaling the symplectic-boson
pairing $\beta(z)\gamma(w)\sim 1/(z-w)$\textup{)} and a \emph{weight
deformation} $\lambda\mapsto\lambda+\epsilon$ \textup{(}moving along
the conformal-weight family\textup{).}  Both are first-order
chiral-bimodule deformations of $\beta\gamma_\lambda$. The
two-dimensional $\ChirHoch^{1}$ is consistent with class
$\mathsf C$'s shadow depth $r_{\max}=4$ \textup{(}quartic shadow,
contact-form rigidity\textup{).}

The breakdown is recorded in the engine and verified for
$\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$, $N \in \{2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 10\}$. The
verification at $N=10$ confirms
$\dim\ChirHoch^{1}(V_k(\mathfrak{sl}_{10})) = 99 = \dim\mathfrak{sl}_{10}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Smooth formal moduli across the standard
landscape; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{prop:smooth-formal-moduli-standard}
\index{deformation theory!unobstructedness}
\index{formal moduli!smoothness}
For every $\cA$ in the standard landscape
$\{\cH_k,\,V_k(\fg),\,\beta\gamma_\lambda,\,\Vir_c,\,\cW_N\,(N\geq 3),
\,\BP_k\}$ at generic parameter, the formal moduli space
$\mathcal{M}_{\cA} = \mathrm{MC}(\Defcyc(\cA))/\mathrm{gauge}$
of chiral $A_\infty$-deformations is \emph{smooth} at $\cA$, with
tangent space $\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$ and dimension as in
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:chirhoch-derivation-types}}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-concentration-E1} the formal
moduli is governed by the truncated $L_\infty$-structure on
$\ChirHoch^{*}(\cA)$, with quadratic obstruction map
$[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]\colon
\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)\otimes\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)
\to\ChirHoch^{2}(\cA)$.
Smoothness at $\cA$ is equivalent to vanishing of the
obstruction class $[\xi,\xi]\in\ChirHoch^{2}(\cA)$ for every
$\xi\in\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$, together with vanishing of all
higher Massey-type obstructions.

For $\Vir_c$, $\cW_N$ at generic $c$, and $\BP_k$ at generic $k$:
$\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)=0$ \textup{(}chiral rigidity, verified in the
chiral-Hochschild engine for $\cW_N$ at $N=3,\ldots,10$\textup{),}
so the obstruction map has empty domain and the formal moduli is
the reduced point.

For $\cH_k$, $V_k(\fg)$, and $\beta\gamma_\lambda$: each
generator $\xi_i$ of $\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$ is realised by an
\emph{actual} smooth one-parameter family
$\{\cA_{\epsilon}\}_{\epsilon\in\mathbb{C}}$ of chiral algebras
extending the trivial deformation. For $\cH_k$ this is the
level rescaling $k\mapsto k+\epsilon$; for $V_k(\fg)$ the
$\dim\fg$-parameter family of inner-gauge orbits of the affine
current $J^a$; for $\beta\gamma_\lambda$ the charge rescaling
and the conformal-weight family
$\lambda\mapsto\lambda+\epsilon$. Each family extends to all
orders in $\epsilon$, so each $\xi_i$ admits a Maurer--Cartan
extension $\Theta(\epsilon)=\xi_i\epsilon+
\Theta_2\epsilon^2+\cdots$ with vanishing obstruction at every
order. By rescaling and superposition, the same holds on the
full $\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$-affine subspace, since the families
commute: levels of distinct generators are independent
parameters. Hence $[\xi,\xi]=0$ in $\ChirHoch^{2}(\cA)$ for
every $\xi$, and all higher Massey obstructions vanish. The
formal moduli is smooth of dimension $\dim\ChirHoch^{1}(\cA)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Meaning of smoothness across archetypes;
\ClaimStatusComputed]
\label{rem:smooth-formal-moduli-archetype}
Proposition~\ref{prop:smooth-formal-moduli-standard} unifies
class~$\mathsf G$, $\mathsf L$, $\mathsf C$, $\mathsf M$
\emph{at the formal-moduli level}: every standard chiral
algebra has unobstructed deformation theory at its base point.
What distinguishes the archetypes is the \emph{dimension} of
the smooth moduli, not its smoothness:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{@{}l c c@{}}
\toprule
Archetype & Family & $\dim\mathcal{M}_{\cA}$ \\
\midrule
$\mathsf G$ Heisenberg & $\cH_k$ & $1$ \\
$\mathsf L$ affine KM & $V_k(\fg)$ & $\dim\fg$ \\
$\mathsf C$ contact & $\beta\gamma_\lambda$ & $2$ \\
$\mathsf M$ minimal & $\Vir_c$ & $0$ \\
$\mathsf M$ minimal & $\cW_N\,(N\geq 3)$ & $0$ \\
$\mathsf M$ subreg.\ & $\BP_k$ & $0$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The non-generic loci (admissible levels for class $\mathsf L$,
minimal models for class $\mathsf M$) are excluded from this
generic-smoothness statement: at these special points the
obstruction theory becomes finite-type completion-theoretic
\textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:hochschild-concentration-class-M-non-generic}\textup{)}.
The class~$\mathsf B$ \textup{(}Mukai--K3 / BKM\textup{)}
chart-level analogue requires a separate analysis with the
Bruinier--Heegner Chern-class reciprocity input and is treated
in Vol~III.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Averaging to symmetric ChirHoch;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}
\index{Hochschild!averaging step}
Let $\cA$ be as in
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-concentration-E1}}, and
assume in addition the $E_{\infty}$-chiral completion
