hypothesis of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}
(flat PBW filtration with commutative-chiral associated
graded). Let
$\mathrm{av}\colon \mathfrak{g}^{E_{1}} \to
\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}$
denote the averaging map from the ordered to the symmetric
chiral convolution dGLA. Then the symmetric coinvariant
Hochschild complex is acyclic in degrees $n\ge 3$, so that
\[
 \ChirHoch^{n}(\cA) \;=\; 0
 \qquad
 \textup{for every } n \notin \{0,1,2\}.
\]
In degrees $0,1,2$ the averaging map identifies the shared
curve-level Ext summands under the PBW diagonal comparison; no
unqualified chain-level equivalence between ordered and symmetric
Hochschild complexes is asserted.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-concentration-E1},
$\ChirHoch^{\mathrm{ord},n}(\cA) = 0$ for $n \notin \{0,1,2\}$.
The $E_{\infty}$-chiral hypothesis provides a
$\Sigma_{n}$-equivariant null-homotopy of the ordered
Hochschild complex in ordered degrees $\ge 3$ at the level
of cochains (the PBW filtration is $\Sigma_{n}$-stable by
construction, and its commutative-chiral associated graded
carries the standard Koszul homotopy equivariantly).
In characteristic zero, finite $\Sigma_n$-coinvariants are exact;
applying them to the equivariant null-homotopy preserves acyclicity
in these degrees. Hence
$\ChirHoch^{n}(\cA) = (\ChirHoch^{\mathrm{ord},n}(\cA))_{\Sigma_{n}}
= 0$ for $n \ge 3$. In degrees $0,1,2$, the diagonal PBW
comparison computes both ordered and symmetric models by the same
curve-level $\cD_X$-Ext summands; this gives the stated low-degree
identification. The bound $n<0$ is trivial.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of the averaging corollary]
\label{rem:hochschild-averaging-scope}
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}}
uses the $E_{\infty}$-chiral completion hypothesis in an
essential way. Outside that hypothesis, for example on an
$E_{1}$-chiral input without a flat PBW filtration such as the
chiral Yangian $Y_{\hbar}(\fg)^{\mathrm{ch}}$, only the ordered bound
of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-concentration-E1}}
survives; the symmetric bound is conjectural (see
Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:hochschild-concentration-E1-only}}).
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[Symmetric concentration for $E_{1}$-chiral
inputs without PBW; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:hochschild-concentration-E1-only}
\index{Hochschild!conjectural symmetric concentration}
\textup{[Regime: ordered $E_{1}$-chiral without PBW.]}
For an $E_{1}$-chiral algebra $\cA$ on a smooth projective
curve $X$ that satisfies ordered bar Koszulity but does
\emph{not} admit a flat PBW filtration with commutative-chiral
associated graded, the symmetric chiral Hochschild
cohomology still vanishes in degrees $n \ge 3$:
\[
 \ChirHoch^{n}(\cA) \;=\; 0
 \qquad
 \textup{for every } n \ge 3.
\]
Equivalently, the averaging map
$\mathrm{av}\colon \ChirHoch^{\mathrm{ord},*}(\cA)
\to \ChirHoch^{*}(\cA)$
is quasi-isomorphic in degrees $\ge 3$ even without
$E_{\infty}$-completion. Test object: the chiral
Yangian $Y_{\hbar}(\fg)^{\mathrm{ch}}$, whose ordered bar
cohomology is supported in ordered degree $1$ but whose
symmetric Hochschild has not been computed directly.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{conjecture}[Chiral Hochschild concentration at admissible
and minimal levels for class M; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:hochschild-concentration-class-M-non-generic}
\index{Hochschild!non-generic level conjecture}
\textup{[Regime: class M, non-generic level.]}
For the Virasoro algebra $\mathrm{Vir}_{c}$ at minimal-model
central charges $c = c_{p,q} = 1 - 6(p-q)^{2}/(pq)$ and for
the principal W-algebra $\Walg^{k}(\fg)$ at admissible
levels, the chiral Hochschild concentration bound of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}} is not a
finite curve-level assertion. The concentration problem is formulated
only in the pro-object or coderived sense:
there exist discrete parameter points where the Shapovalov
form degenerates and the completed obstruction ambient allows
degree-$3$ classes in the completed or coderived diagonal obstruction
complex
$RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{cod},\Delta}(\cA)$ before passing to the
perfect finite-window quotient used in Theorem~H. This is not a
claim about the curve-level Vol~I group $\ChirHoch^3(\cA)$ on the
Theorem~H domain. A rigorous statement at these points requires
either a coderived reinterpretation of the simple-quotient complex or
a case-by-case vanishing argument invoking the concrete
Kac-determinant structure.
Unconditional $\{0,1,2\}$ concentration for class M is
proved only at generic level
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:virasoro-hochschild}}
and
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:w-algebra-hochschild}}\textup{)};
the critical level $k = -h^{\vee}$ is excluded from this finite
Theorem~H lane. Bar-object PBW Koszulness of the universal affine
algebra does not supply the missing finite-window perfectness. The
obstruction is finite-type and completion-theoretic: the
Feigin--Frenkel centre contributes an
infinite-dimensional $\ChirHoch^0$, the diagonal Hochschild complex is
not a perfect finite-window object, and a completed or coderived
critical-level Hochschild theorem is a separate statement
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:critical-level-dimensional-divergence}}\textup{)}.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Meaning of ``$E_{1}$'' in the label: spectral-sequence
page, not E$_{1}$-chiral input]
\label{rem:E1-scope-hochschild-concentration}
The subscript $E_{1}$ in
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-concentration-E1} refers to the
\emph{first page of the collision-depth spectral sequence} on the
ordered Fulton--MacPherson compactification
$\overline{C}^{\mathrm{ord}}_{p+2}(X)$, on which the fibrewise
pure-braid Orlik--Solomon homotopy acts. It does not refer to
E$_{1}$-chiral input algebras in the sense of the Yangian. The
hypothesis of this theorem is the PBW criterion
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion}}\textup{)},
which is an E$_{\infty}$-chiral condition: it requires a flat PBW
filtration whose associated graded is a commutative chiral algebra.
For an E$_{1}$-chiral input such as the chiral Yangian
$Y_{\hbar}(\fg)^{\mathrm{ch}}$, the correct analogue is the
ordered bar Koszulity statement of the ordered associative
chiral Koszul-duality formalism \textup{(}see the ordered
treatment of Kac--Moody and Yangian in the appendix
\texttt{ordered\_associative\_chiral\_kd.tex}\textup{)}, which
asserts concentration of the ordered bar cohomology in ordered
degree~$1$; the passage from ordered bar Koszulity to a
symmetric-side $\{0,1,2\}$ bound on $\ChirHoch^{*}$ requires an
averaging step that is genuine only on E$_{\infty}$-chiral
completions.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Why the collapse is nontrivial]
\label{rem:fm-collapse-nontrivial}
The collapse of Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse} is the
essential content of Theorem~H beyond a formal degree count.
The bigraded definition places cochains on spaces
$\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ of dimension~$p+2$, which grows without
bound. Without the Koszul hypothesis, the Arnold-algebra
contributions from higher collision strata can survive to the
$E_2$-page, so the chiral Hochschild cohomology is no longer
controlled by a uniform $[0,2]$ amplitude bound. PBW Koszulness provides the
input that kills these contributions: the
Shelton--Yuzvinsky contracting homotopy on the pure-braid
Orlik--Solomon algebra, transported through the chiral quadratic
Koszul map, annihilates the positive Arnold fibre classes and
leaves only the curve-level Ext with amplitude~$[0,2]$ from the
single complex dimension of~$X$.

For comparison: the \emph{topological} Hochschild complex of an
$E_1$-algebra~$A$ over a point has no $\mathcal D_X$-Ext amplitude
coming from a curve; its cohomological range is controlled by the
algebra~$A$, not by Theorem~H. The chiral setting inserts a complex
curve~$X$, and each local configuration space $\FM_m(\C)$ contributes
Arnold cohomology that must be killed. The FM-formality spectral
sequence is the mechanism by which PBW/Arnold collapse leaves only
the curve-level Ext amplitude~$[0,2]$.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Chiral Hochschild descent; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{lem:chirhoch-descent}
\index{chiral Hochschild!descent from bar}
Let $\cA$ be a PBW chiral Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$, satisfying the $E_{\infty}$-chiral completion hypothesis
of Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}} and
the geometric--algebraic comparison hypotheses of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-bar-cobar}}. The derived chiral
Hochschild complex $RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ is computed by the
two-sided diagonal bar resolution and is filtered quasi-isomorphic to
the Verdier-dual diagonal-bar coefficient object
\[
\mathsf{DHH}_{\Sigma}(\cA)
:=
\bigl(\mathbb{D}_{\Ran}\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}_X(\cA)\bigr)_{\Sigma,\Delta}.
\]
Here $(-)_{\Sigma,\Delta}$ denotes totalized $\Sigma_n$-coinvariants
in bar degree~$n$, with the two external Hochschild marked points kept
as the diagonal bimodule legs. Concretely, on this locus there is a
natural filtered quasi-isomorphism of chain complexes
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-descent}
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;
\mathsf{DHH}_{\Sigma}(\cA).
\end{equation}
If
\[
\cA^i := H^*\bigl(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr),
\qquad
\cA^! := \mathbb{D}_X(\cA^i),
\]
then the associated graded of~$\mathsf{DHH}_{\Sigma}(\cA)$ under the
PBW/Arnold collision filtration has degree-$p$ coefficient
\[
R\operatorname{Hom}_{\cD_X}\bigl((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X\bigr).
\]
Thus the comparison chain used by Theorem~H is
\[
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\cA^i
\;\xrightarrow{\ \mathbb{D}_X\ }\;
\cA^!,
\]
with no direct identification of the bar coalgebra, the Hochschild
cochain object, or the bar-cobar inverse with the Koszul dual algebra.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-bar-cobar} computes the derived
chiral Hochschild complex by the two-sided diagonal bar resolution
\[
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\simeq
R\mathrm{Hom}_{\cA^e}(\cA,\cA)
\simeq
\mathrm{Hom}_{\cA^e}
\bigl(\cA\otimes\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\otimes\cA,\cA\bigr).
\]
The FM/Verdier pairing identifies a diagonal bimodule functional on
the middle bar coalgebra with a $\Sigma_n$-coinvariant section of
$\mathbb{D}_{\Ran}\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ in bar degree~$n$; the two
outer $\cA$-factors are the two boundary marked points in the
Hochschild configuration. This gives the filtered comparison
\eqref{eq:chirhoch-descent}; applying cohomology gives
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$.

The $E_{\infty}$-chiral completion makes ordered-to-symmetric
coinvariants compatible with the PBW filtration. On the Koszul locus,
Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration} identifies the associated graded of
the bar coalgebra with its bar cohomology coalgebra
$\cA^i=H^*(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA))$. Degreewise Verdier duality on
the curve then gives
$\cA^! = \mathbb D_X(\cA^i)$, and the degree-$p$ coefficient of the
surviving collision spectral sequence is
$R\operatorname{Hom}_{\cD_X}((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X)$. Thus the bar
coalgebra, the Hochschild cochain object, the bar cohomology coalgebra,
and the Koszul dual algebra remain separated by the chain
\[
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\to \cA^i \xrightarrow{\mathbb{D}_X}\cA^!.
\]
The bar--cobar counit is used only to prove that the two-sided bar
object resolves the diagonal bimodule; it does not identify
$\Omega\barB(\cA)$ with the Koszul dual algebra.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Theorem H exactness criterion]
\label{rem:theorem-H-filter-exactness}
The proof of Theorem~H uses three filtrations, and the theorem is true
on the common locus where all three are exact in the following sense.
First, the collision-depth filtration
$F_{\mathrm{coll}}$ on the FM compactification
$\overline C_{p+2}(X)$ has spectral sequence
\[
E_1^{a,b}(p)
=
H^{a+b}\bigl(\operatorname{gr}^{a}_{F_{\mathrm{coll}}}
CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr)
\Longrightarrow
H^{a+b}CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA),
\]
and the PBW/Arnold contraction identifies its surviving page as
\[
E_2^{a,p}(p)
\cong
\operatorname{Ext}_{\cD_X}^{a}\bigl((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X\bigr),
\qquad
E_2^{a,b}(p)=0\quad (b\ne p),
\]
with $d_r^{\mathrm{coll}}=0$ for $r\ge2$. Second, the bar-degree
filtration $F_{\mathrm{bar}}$ on the direct-sum totalization
$\operatorname{Tot}^{\oplus}_{p\ge0}
\bigl(CH^{p,\bullet}_{\mathrm{ch}}[-p]\bigr)$
transports this support to total cohomological degrees
$0,1,2$. Third, the conformal-weight/PBW filtration
$F_{\mathrm{wt}}$ is first applied in finite weight windows and then
completed; the inverse system is required to satisfy the
Mittag--Leffler condition, so the obstruction term
\[
\lambda^1_n(\cA)
:=
R^1\!\varprojlim_N
H^{n-1}\!\left(
F_{\mathrm{wt}}^{N}RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)/
F_{\mathrm{wt}}^{N+1}RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\right)
\]
vanishes.

Equivalently, the theorem excludes exactly the following failure
modes. Positive Arnold fibre classes
$\epsilon_{\mathrm{Arn}}\in E_1^{*,>0}$ must be killed by the
Shelton--Yuzvinsky homotopy transported through the chiral quadratic
Koszul map; higher collision differentials
$d_r^{\mathrm{coll}}(\epsilon)$ for $r\ge2$ must vanish; the
completion defect $\lambda^1_n(\cA)$ must vanish in every degree; and
the Verdier/perfectness cone
\[
\mathfrak p_\cA
:=
\operatorname{Cone}\!\left(
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\longrightarrow
R\operatorname{Hom}(RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!),\omega_X[2])
\right)
\]
must be acyclic. On the generic PBW finite-type lanes these four
terms vanish by the preceding lemmas. At critical affine level,
bar-object PBW Koszulness of the universal affine algebra does not
repair the finite-type failure: the Feigin--Frenkel centre populates
$\ChirHoch^0$ infinitely and the finite-window/perfectness condition
fails. At admissible, minimal, and logarithmic simple-quotient loci,
null-vector and Jordan-block phenomena enter the Li-bar
$E_2$-page or in $\lambda^1_n(\cA)$; those cases require a coderived
or case-by-case theorem and are not consequences of Theorem~H.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Koszul duality for chiral Hochschild cohomology
\textup{(}Theorem~H\textup{)}; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:main-koszul-hoch}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!Koszul duality|textbf}
\index{Theorem H!structural form via Koszul Reflection}

\textup{[Regime: quadratic on the Koszul locus
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}
\textup{[Excludes critical level $k = -h^\vee$ for affine
Kac--Moody algebras; see
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:critical-level-dimensional-divergence}}.]}

\textit{The Hochschild theory used here is the chiral
$\ChirHoch^*$, distinct from topological $\mathrm{THH}(R)$
and categorical $\mathrm{HH}^*_{\mathrm{cat}}$
(Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:three-hochschild-discipline}}).}
The statement is the trace shadow of the Koszul Reflection
$K^{2}\simeq\mathrm{id}$ of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:koszul-reflection}} read on the chiral
derived centre $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$.

For every PBW chiral Koszul datum~$\cA$
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:chiral-koszul-morphism})} with
dual~$\cA^!$ on a smooth projective curve~$X$, whose diagonal
chiral Hochschild complexes for $\cA$ and $\cA^!$ are perfect in
the holonomic $\mathcal D_X$-module derived category and have
finite-dimensional graded realizations, satisfying the
$E_{\infty}$-chiral completion hypothesis of
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}} and lying
away from critical affine levels and the minimal/admissible simple
quotient points recorded in the non-generic class-\(\mathsf M\)
scope discussion above,
and with all complexes first taken in finite conformal-weight windows and
then completed with respect to the conformal-weight/PBW filtration
under the Mittag--Leffler condition recorded in
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:theorem-H-filter-exactness}},
the bigraded chiral Hochschild complex
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:bigraded-hochschild})} satisfies
the \emph{derived-level} duality:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:hochschild-H-derived}
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;\simeq\;
R\mathrm{Hom}\bigl(RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!),\, \omega_X[2]\bigr).
\end{equation}
The non-generic class-\(\mathsf M\) discussion above is an exclusion
from the theorem's domain, not a proof input.
The totalization is the direct-sum totalization in bar degree before
weight completion; replacing it by an unrestricted product
totalization is a different completed/coderived statement.
On cohomology:
\[
\ChirHoch^n(\mathcal{A}) \cong \ChirHoch^{2-n}(\mathcal{A}^!)^{\vee} \otimes \omega_X.
\]
The shift by~$2$ is the output of the
Fulton--MacPherson collapse
\textup{(}Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}}
and
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}}\textup{)}:
the FM-formality spectral sequence collapses the tower of
configuration spaces $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ to the
curve-level $\mathcal{D}_X$-Ext via the PBW/Arnold contraction, so the
geometric shift~$[p+2]$ on $\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$ is cancelled
by the totalization shift~$[-p]$ and only the base-curve
shift~$[2]$ survives.
The $\omega_X$ twist encodes the dualizing sheaf.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Lemma~\ref{lem:chirhoch-descent} supplies filtered
quasi-isomorphisms from the derived chiral Hochschild complexes to
the $\Sigma$-coinvariant descents of the homotopy Koszul dual
factorization algebras:
\[
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\simeq
\bigl((\cA)^!_\infty\bigr)_{\Sigma},
\qquad
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!)
\simeq
\bigl((\cA^!)^!_\infty\bigr)_{\Sigma}.
\]
The same lemma records the corrected comparison chain
\[
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\longrightarrow
\cA^i:=H^*\bigl(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\bigr)
\xrightarrow{\ \mathbb{D}_X\ }
\cA^!,
\]
and likewise with $\cA$ and $\cA^!$ interchanged.
Thus the bar coalgebra, the dual coalgebra, and the Koszul dual
algebra stay separated throughout the argument.

Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation} to the filtered
complexes $RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ and $RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!)$.
At each bar degree~$p$, the corresponding $E_2$-terms are the
curve-level Ext groups of the degree-$p$ pieces of the two Koszul
dual algebras.
By the corrected comparison chains
\[
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\to \cA^i \xrightarrow{\mathbb{D}_X}\cA^!,
\qquad
\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!)\to (\cA^!)^i \xrightarrow{\mathbb{D}_X}\cA,
\]
the coefficient systems on the two $E_2$-pages are exchanged by
curve-level Verdier duality.
Curve-level Verdier duality therefore gives, bar degree by bar degree,
\[
E_2^{r,p}(\cA)
\;\cong\;
\bigl(E_2^{2-r,p}(\cA^!)\bigr)^\vee \otimes \omega_X.
\]
Because the collision-depth spectral sequences of
Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation} degenerate at~$E_2$,
the same duality passes to the abutments.
The perfectness hypothesis is the point at which the derived
$R\mathrm{Hom}$ expression and the cohomological linear duals are
legitimate; without it the statement must be made in a
completed or coderived ambient.
The uniform shift is exactly the shift~$[2]$ computed there, so
\[
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\;\simeq\;
R\mathrm{Hom}\bigl(RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA^!),\,\omega_X[2]\bigr),
\]
which is~\eqref{eq:hochschild-H-derived}. Taking cohomology gives
\[
\ChirHoch^n(\cA)
\;\cong\;
\ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee \otimes \omega_X.
\]

The same degree reflection is visible deformation-theoretically:
the Kodaira--Spencer map
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:kodaira-spencer-chiral-complete}}\textup{)}
and the module Koszul duality equivalence
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality}}\textup{)}
identify the tangent complexes on the two sides, while
Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation} supplies the same
curve-level shift~$[2]$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Diagonal, FM, Verdier]
The argument uses three independent inputs: the diagonal two-sided bar
resolution, PBW/FM collapse of the collision-depth spectral sequence,
and curve-level Verdier duality. The bar--cobar quasi-isomorphism
(Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}) supplies the diagonal
resolution; it is inversion $\Omega\barB(\cA)\simeq\cA$, not the
identification of $\Omega\barB(\cA)$ with the Koszul dual algebra.
The Kodaira--Spencer map for Koszul pairs
(Theorem~\ref{thm:kodaira-spencer-chiral-complete}) gives the
deformation-theoretic reading after the Hochschild duality has been
proved.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Polynomial growth of chiral Hochschild cohomology
\textup{(}Theorem~H, growth clause\textup{)}; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!polynomial growth|textbf}
\textup{[Regime: quadratic on the Koszul locus
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

Let $\cA$ be a PBW chiral Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$, with $E_{\infty}$-chiral completion as in
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:hochschild-averaging-symmetric}}, away from
critical affine levels and from the minimal/admissible simple quotient
points of the non-generic class-\(\mathsf M\) scope,
and let $\cA^!$ denote its Koszul dual. Assume the same
finite-type/perfectness hypotheses as in
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}, so that the displayed
dimensions are dimensions of finite graded pieces. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Concentration \textup{(}cohomological amplitude, not
 virtual dimension\textup{)}.}\;
 $\ChirHoch^n(\cA) = 0$ for $n < 0$ and $n > 2$.
 The nonvanishing range is $0 \leq n \leq 2$.

\item \emph{Polynomial growth.}\;
 The Hochschild--Hilbert series
 \[
 P_{\cA}(t)
 \;:=\;
 \sum_{n \geq 0} \dim \ChirHoch^n(\cA)\,t^n
 \]
 is a polynomial of degree at most~$2$. More precisely,
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:hoch-hilbert-polynomial}
 P_{\cA}(t)
 \;=\;
 \dim Z(\cA)
 + \dim \ChirHoch^1(\cA)\,t
 + \dim Z(\cA^!)\,t^2,
 \end{equation}
 where $Z(\cA) = \ChirHoch^0(\cA)$ is the center, and the
 $t^2$-coefficient is the dimension of the Verdier-dual centre
 $Z(\cA^!)^\vee\otimes\omega_X$ supplied by
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}.

\item \emph{Koszul functoriality.}\;
 The polynomial $P_{\cA}(t)$ is determined by the Koszul dual pair:
 \[
 P_{\cA}(t) + P_{\cA^!}(t)
 \;=\;
 (\dim Z(\cA) + \dim Z(\cA^!))(1+t^2)
 + (\dim \ChirHoch^1(\cA) + \dim \ChirHoch^1(\cA^!))\,t,
 \]
 and the palindromic duality
 $P_{\cA}(t) = t^2\,P_{\cA^!}(t^{-1})$
 holds under the same Koszul-locus hypotheses
 \textup{(}the Koszul duality
 $\ChirHoch^n(\cA) \cong \ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee \otimes \omega_X$
 from Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}
 exchanges the constant and leading coefficients).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(a): fix a bar degree~$p$.
Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}, with the
configuration-space collapse justified by
Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}, furnishes a
first-quadrant spectral sequence
\[
E_2^{r,s}(p)=0 \text{ for } s\neq p,
\qquad
E_2^{r,p}(p)\cong
\Ext_{\mathcal{D}_X}^r\!\bigl((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X\bigr),
\]
and this spectral sequence degenerates at~$E_2$.
Because $X$ is a smooth projective curve,
\[
\Ext_{\mathcal{D}_X}^r\!\bigl((\cA^!)_p,\omega_X\bigr)=0
\qquad\text{for } r\notin\{0,1,2\},
\]
so every bar-degree summand of the Hochschild total complex has
cohomological amplitude~$[0,2]$.
The totalization amplitude is then bounded by
Lemma~\ref{lem:totalization-amplitude}, which transports the
per-bar-degree amplitude to the totalization. Hence
$\ChirHoch^n(\cA)=0$ for $n<0$ and $n>2$.
Thus the only possible nonzero degrees are $0$, $1$, and~$2$.

Part~(b): part~(a) implies that $P_\cA(t)$ is a polynomial of
degree at most~$2$. Its constant term is
$\dim \ChirHoch^0(\cA)=\dim Z(\cA)$. For the quadratic term,
set $n=2$ in Theorem~\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}:
\[
\ChirHoch^2(\cA)
\;\cong\;
\ChirHoch^0(\cA^!)^\vee \otimes \omega_X.
\]
Because $\omega_X$ is a line bundle on the fixed curve~$X$, it
changes the geometric twist but not the dimension of the finite
graded coefficient counted by $P_\cA(t)$. Therefore
\[
\dim \ChirHoch^2(\cA)
\;=\;
\dim \ChirHoch^0(\cA^!)
\;=\;
\dim Z(\cA^!),
\]
which is exactly~\eqref{eq:hoch-hilbert-polynomial}.

Part~(c): applying Theorem~\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch} in degrees
$n=0,1,2$ gives
\[
\dim \ChirHoch^0(\cA)=\dim \ChirHoch^2(\cA^!),
\qquad
\dim \ChirHoch^1(\cA)=\dim \ChirHoch^1(\cA^!),
\qquad
\dim \ChirHoch^2(\cA)=\dim \ChirHoch^0(\cA^!).
\]
If
\[
P_\cA(t)=a_0+a_1 t+a_2 t^2,
\qquad
P_{\cA^!}(t)=a_2+a_1 t+a_0 t^2,
\]
then
\[
t^2 P_{\cA^!}(t^{-1})
= a_0 + a_1 t + a_2 t^2
= P_\cA(t),
\]
which proves the palindromic identity. Adding the two degree-$2$
polynomials termwise gives the displayed formula for
$P_\cA(t)+P_{\cA^!}(t)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Deformation-theoretic reading of the amplitude]
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}\textup{(a)}
has a deformation-theoretic interpretation after the
FM/bar-collision proof has supplied the amplitude bound.

By Definition~\ref{def:cyclic-deformation-elementary}, the formal
deformation problem of~$\cA$ is governed by the cyclic deformation
object. In the tangent-complex indexing convenient for the formal
moduli problem, one reads off the infinitesimal data as
\[
Z(\cA)=\ChirHoch^0(\cA),\qquad
T_\cA=\ChirHoch^1(\cA),\qquad
\operatorname{Obs}_\cA=\ChirHoch^2(\cA).
\]
Thus $\ChirHoch^1(\cA)$ controls first-order tangent directions and
$\ChirHoch^2(\cA)$ controls obstructions. The degree-$0$ term is the
center; for the connected examples of Theorem~H this is the scalar
identity line. This is the deformation-theoretic reindexing of the
usual Gerstenhaber cochain grading.

The dimension bound is then a local-to-global statement. The chiral
deformation object is valued in holonomic $\cD_X$-modules, so on a
smooth curve the derived global-sections functor contributes at most
one cohomological step. The chiral product itself contributes one
internal deformation step because the local deformation problem is
binary. In the unshifted Hochschild grading this gives
\[
[0,1+1]=[0,2].
\]
This is the shadow of the proved FM collapse, not an independent
proof: without the PBW/Koszul contraction of the Arnold fibre
classes, the local binary deformation count does not rule out
cohomology created by the unbounded tower
$\overline{C}_{p+2}(X)$.

Once one knows that the deformation problem is finite-dimensional on
the Koszul locus, only the three groups
$\ChirHoch^0(\cA)$, $\ChirHoch^1(\cA)$, and $\ChirHoch^2(\cA)$ can
contribute. Therefore
\[
P_\cA(t)=\sum_{n\ge 0}\dim \ChirHoch^n(\cA)\,t^n
\]
is automatically a polynomial of degree at most~$2$:
\[
P_\cA(t)
=
\dim Z(\cA)
+\dim \ChirHoch^1(\cA)\,t
+\dim \ChirHoch^2(\cA)\,t^2.
\]
Theorem~\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch} then identifies the quadratic
coefficient with $\dim Z(\cA^!)$, recovering
\eqref{eq:hoch-hilbert-polynomial}. Outside the PBW Koszul and
finite-type/perfectness regime, the displayed deformation reading is
only the standard indexing of the obstruction theory; it supplies no
concentration theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Geometric substrate (Volume~II)]
\label{rem:theorem-h-lagrangian}
\index{Lagrangian self-intersection!Theorem H}
Volume~II interprets this as the HKR theorem for Lagrangian
embeddings: the chiral Hochschild complex is the normal complex of
$\mathcal{L} \hookrightarrow \mathcal{M}$, and the polynomial
growth bound reflects the finite excess dimension of
$\mathfrak{S} = \mathcal{L} \times_{\mathcal{M}} \mathcal{L}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Chiral vs classical Hochschild: structural vs dimensional]
\label{rem:critical-level-dimensional-divergence}
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth} is a specifically
\emph{chiral} result: the concentration in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$
follows from the de~Rham amplitude bound
$[0, 2\dim_\bC X] = [0, 2]$ for $\cD_X$-module Ext on a curve.
Three invariants must be distinguished:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$: chiral Hochschild cochains.
 Concentrated in $\{0,1,2\}$ (this theorem).
 For the Heisenberg: $\dim = 3$.
\item $\HH^*(A_{\mathrm{mode}}, A_{\mathrm{mode}})$: classical
 Hochschild cochains of the mode algebra (an associative algebra
 in $\Vect$). For the Weyl algebra:
 $\HH^0(A_1) = \bC$, $\HH^n(A_1) = 0$ for $n \ge 1$
 (total dimension~$1$). This is \emph{more} concentrated
 than~$\ChirHoch^*$, not less.
\item $H^*_{\mathrm{cont}}(\mathrm{Lie}(\cA); \bC)$:
 Gel'fand--Fuchs continuous Lie cohomology of the
 positive-mode subalgebra
 $L_+ = \bigoplus_{n \ge 1} \bC \cdot L_n$.
 For the Virasoro: $H^*(L_+; \bC) = \bC[c_2]$
 with $|c_2| = 2$ (Goncharova; Fuks,
 \emph{Cohomology of Infinite-Dimensional Lie Algebras},
 Theorem~1.4.3): a polynomial ring, unbounded.
\end{enumerate}
At \emph{generic} level, $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$ and
$\HH^*(A_{\mathrm{mode}})$ have the same cohomological
dimension (both finite, both concentrated). The genuine
difference is \emph{structural}: $\ChirHoch^*$ carries an
$\Etwo$-algebra structure with spectral parameters from the
chiral endomorphism operad, while
$\HH^*(A_{\mathrm{mode}})$ carries $\Etwo$ from the Deligne
conjecture (abstract, no spectral data).

The \emph{only} regime where the two genuinely diverge in
\emph{dimension} is the \textbf{critical level} $k = -h^\vee$:
here $\ChirHoch^*$ becomes infinite-dimensional
(the Feigin--Frenkel centre
$\mathrm{Fun}(\mathrm{Op}_{\fg^\vee}(D))$ populates $\ChirHoch^0$),
while $\HH^*(A_{\mathrm{mode}})$ remains finite.
This is the scope boundary of Theorem~H: Koszulness by itself is
not enough. At critical level the generic finite-type/perfectness
and completion hypotheses needed by the FM-tower collapse fail, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse} no longer supplies a
finite three-term chiral Hochschild complex.
This is a finite-type and perfectness failure, not a proved
degree-$3$ class at critical level; such a claim requires a
completed critical-level Hochschild computation.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Deformation-obstruction exchange at genus \texorpdfstring{$0$}{0}; \ClaimStatusConditional]\label{cor:def-obs-exchange-genus0}
\index{deformation-obstruction!genus-0 exchange}
Let $(\mathcal{A}, \mathcal{A}^!)$ be a PBW chiral Koszul pair on a
smooth projective curve~$X$, satisfying the $E_{\infty}$-completion,
generic/perfectness, and non-critical hypotheses of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}. Then the degree-$2$
endpoint of the unshifted curve-level chiral Hochschild complex of
$\mathcal{A}$ is dual to the ordinary chiral centre of
$\mathcal{A}^!$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:def-obs-genus0}
\ChirHoch^2(\mathcal{A}) \;\cong\; \ChirHoch^0(\mathcal{A}^!)^{\vee} \otimes \omega_X.
\end{equation}
In Gerstenhaber product-deformation grading this is the
product-deformation endpoint; in the shifted formal-moduli convention
used for the MC problem, $\ChirHoch^1(\mathcal A)$ is the tangent
space and $\ChirHoch^2(\mathcal A)$ is the primary obstruction target.
More generally, the genus-$0$ curve-level chiral deformation complex of
$\mathcal{A}$ is dual to the corresponding curve-level obstruction
complex of $\mathcal{A}^!$ with a shift by~$2$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Set $n = 2$ in Theorem~\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}:
\[
\ChirHoch^2(\mathcal{A})
\cong
\ChirHoch^{0}(\mathcal{A}^!)^\vee \otimes \omega_X .
\]
Here $\ChirHoch^2(\mathcal{A})$ is the curve-level chiral
product-deformation endpoint, equivalently the primary obstruction
target after shifting to the formal-moduli convention, and
$\ChirHoch^0(\mathcal{A}^!)=Z(\mathcal{A}^!)$ is the ordinary
chiral centre of the Koszul dual. The statement does not apply to
topological Hochschild, categorical Hochschild, or product-ambient
CY Hochschild complexes.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}\label{rem:def-obs-higher-genus}
At genus $g \geq 1$, the exchange is Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main} (Theorem~C): $Q_g(\mathcal{A}) \oplus Q_g(\mathcal{A}^!) \cong H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A}))$. The genus-$0$ corollary is the seed from which higher-genus complementarity grows via the Faber--Pandharipande mechanism (Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}).
\end{remark}

\begin{example}[Heisenberg specialization]\label{ex:heisenberg-curved-specialization}
For the Heisenberg algebra $\mathcal{H}_k$, the curved
$A_\infty$ structure on the Koszul dual
$\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ has
$m_0 = -k \cdot \omega$ and $m_n = 0$ for $n \geq 3$: the curvature is
the entire obstruction, with no higher operations
(\S\ref{sec:frame-genus1}). This is the simplest nontrivial instance
of the deformation-obstruction exchange above:
$\ChirHoch^2(\mathcal{H}_k) = \mathbb{C}$ is the degree-$2$ endpoint
recording the level-curvature obstruction target, dual to
$\ChirHoch^0(\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*))^\vee \otimes \omega_X =
\mathbb{C}$ (the center of the dual).
\end{example}


%================================================================
% FORMALITY, MODULI, AND OPERADIC PERSPECTIVES ON KOSZULNESS
%================================================================

\subsection{Formality, moduli, and operadic perspectives on Koszulness}
\label{subsec:formality-moduli-operadic}

The modular
convolution algebra $\gAmod$ carries the universal Maurer--Cartan
element $\Theta_{\cA}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}); every structural property
of~$\cA$ is a property of~$\Theta_{\cA}$. Four
formality-type conditions on~$\gAmod$ and their consequences for
Koszulness follow.

\medskip

\begin{proposition}[Conditional $\Etwo$-formality criterion for chiral Hochschild cohomology;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{prop:e2-formality-hochschild}
\index{formality!$\Etwo$-chiral Hochschild}
\index{Hochschild cohomology!$\Etwo$-formality}
Let $\cA$ be a chirally Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$. Assume a brace-compatible contraction, equivalently an
$\Etwo$ quasi-isomorphism from $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$ to its
cohomology Gerstenhaber algebra. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$ is formal as an $\Etwo$-algebra:
 the $\Etwo$ quasi-isomorphism type of $\ChirHoch^*(\cA)$ is
 determined by the graded algebra $H^*(\ChirHoch(\cA))$ with its
 cup product and degree-$1$ bracket.

\item All higher $\Etwo$-operations \textup{(}braces of
 degree~$\geq 3$, Massey products, $A_\infty$ corrections\textup{)}
 are cohomologically trivial.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Choose the brace-compatible contraction in the hypothesis. Homological
transfer then identifies the $\Etwo$-algebra
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$ with the cohomology Gerstenhaber algebra
equipped with the transferred $\Etwo$-structure. The additional
hypothesis says precisely that this transferred structure is
quasi-isomorphic, as an $\Etwo$-algebra, to the strict Gerstenhaber
model determined by the cup product and bracket. This gives~(i).

For~(ii), the same $\Etwo$ quasi-isomorphism sends each higher brace
or Massey operation of arity at least~$3$ to zero in the strict
Gerstenhaber model; equivalently, those operations are coboundaries in
the original brace dg algebra. Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}
supplies only the support bound
$\ChirHoch^n(\cA)=0$ for $n\notin\{0,1,2\}$. That bound is compatible
with the transfer, but it is not the source of the contraction and does
not imply $\Etwo$-formality by itself.
\end{proof}

\section{Beilinson--Drinfeld diagonal factorization cochains and
chiral Hochschild}
\label{sec:bd-fact-vs-chirhoch}

\index{factorization cohomology!vs.\ chiral Hochschild|textbf}
\index{Beilinson--Drinfeld!factorization cohomology comparison|textbf}
\index{Ran space!diagonal bimodule}

There are two a priori distinct Ext-theoretic cohomologies of a
chiral algebra~$\cA$ on a smooth projective
curve~$X$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the \emph{chiral Hochschild cohomology}
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA) =
\Ext^\bullet_{\cA^e}(\cA,\cA)$
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:chiral-hochschild-complex}},
geometric FM model;
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:chirHoch-Ext}} in
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:koszul-pair-structure}},
algebraic $\Ext$-model\textup{)},
which is chain-level and native to
$\mathcal{D}_X$-module theory;
\item the \emph{Beilinson--Drinfeld factorization cohomology}
of the diagonal bimodule,
\[
\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)
\;:=\;
R\mathrm{Hom}_{\operatorname{Fact}(X)}
\bigl(\cA,\, \cA^{\mathrm{diag}}\bigr),
\]
the derived $\operatorname{Fact}(X)$-internal Hom from $\cA$ (as
factorization algebra on $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$) to itself as
a factorization bimodule
\textup{(}Beilinson--Drinfeld~\textup{\cite[\S3.4]{BD04}};
Francis--Gaitsgory
$(\infty,1)$-enhancement~\textup{\cite[\S5.5.2]{HA}},
Ayala--Francis~\textup{\cite[\S3-\S4]{AF15}}\textup{)}, which
is $(\infty,1)$-categorical and native to $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
\end{enumerate}
The question of when these coincide is structurally parallel to
the bar--cobar identification
$\Bbar_X(\cA) \simeq \int_X\cA$
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:bar-fh}} in
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:bar-cobar}}\textup{)} and its dual
$\Omega_X(\cC) \simeq \int^X\cC$
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:cobar-fh}} in
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:bar-cobar}}\textup{)}: bar/cobar are
factorization homology/cohomology of the unit bimodule when the
BD comparison hypotheses are satisfied, whereas
$\ChirHoch$ and $\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)$
are the cohomological Ext of the diagonal bimodule.

\begin{theorem}[BD diagonal factorization cochains versus chiral
Hochschild; \ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:bd-fact-vs-chirhoch}
\index{Theorem H!BD factorization cohomology refinement}
\textup{[Regime: quadratic on the Koszul locus
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})};
bounded-below $\cA$; smooth projective curve~$X$;
$\dim_{\mathbb{C}} X = 1$;
ambient: raw bounded
$\mathcal{D}_X$-module complexes; excludes critical
level $k=-h^\vee$; assumes diagonal Ran--FM descent as stated
below.]}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral Koszul algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$. There is a natural comparison morphism
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bd-chirhoch-comparison}
c_{\cA}\colon
\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)
\end{equation}
in the derived category of $\mathcal{D}_X$-modules on
$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$, induced by restricting a factorization
cochain to its diagonal component and descending to the FM model.
Assume that the diagonal Ran--FM descent comparison for~$\cA$
is effective: the finite-subset filtration on
$\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)$ and the
collision-depth filtration on the FM model admit a filtered
comparison whose associated-graded map is the two-sided chiral
bar resolution of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-bar-cobar}},
and this associated-graded comparison is a quasi-isomorphism after
the PBW/Arnold contraction of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}}. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Chain-level qualification.}\;
The comparison $c_{\cA}$ is \emph{not} a chain-level
isomorphism for a generic chiral algebra~$\cA$: the left-hand
side carries the $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$-theoretic
$(\infty,1)$-categorical enhancement from
Francis--Gaitsgory~\textup{\cite[\S5.5.2]{HA}}, while the
right-hand side is chain-level via the FM compactification
$\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$. The two models agree only after
passing through the filtered diagonal comparison; chain-level
equality fails because the Ran-colimit differential carries
simplicial-like boundary contributions that are only cancelled
on cohomology after FM collapse
\textup{(}Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}},
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse}}\textup{)}.
\item \emph{Cohomological isomorphism under diagonal descent.}\;
The induced map on cohomology
\[
H^n(c_{\cA})\colon
H^n\bigl(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)\bigr)
\;\xrightarrow{\ \cong\ }\;
\ChirHoch^n(\cA)
\qquad (n \in \mathbb{Z})
\]
is an isomorphism for every~$n$. In particular, under the same
diagonal descent hypothesis, BD factorization cohomology of the
diagonal bimodule has cohomological amplitude~$[0,2]$:
$H^n(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA))=0$
for $n\notin\{0,1,2\}$.
\item \emph{$(\infty,1)$-categorical enhancement.}\;
Under the same diagonal descent hypothesis, the filtered
quasi-isomorphism represented by $c_{\cA}$ becomes an equivalence
\[
\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)
\;\simeq\;
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)
\]
in the $(\infty,1)$-category
$\mathrm{D}(\mathrm{Fact}(X))$. This is not a formal consequence of
factorization homology alone; the diagonal bimodule descent map is
the extra input.
\item \emph{Class dependence.}\;
The conclusion applies on the generic PBW lanes of the standard
archetypes \textup{G/L/C/M} precisely where the diagonal Ran--FM
descent hypothesis above is available from a bounded two-sided
bar resolution: Heisenberg, affine Kac--Moody away from the critical
level, $\beta\gamma$, and the generic universal
Virasoro/principal $\mathcal W$ lanes. Critical affine level and
minimal/admissible simple quotients are excluded from this clause and
belong to the coderived or non-generic class-\(\mathsf M\) scope.
\item \emph{Verdier self-duality.}\;
If the diagonal descent comparison is Verdier-compatible for both
$\cA$ and~$\cA^!$, then the transported cohomological comparison
intertwines the curve-level Verdier duality of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}} and yields
\[
H^n\bigl(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)\bigr)
\;\cong\;
H^{2-n}\bigl(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA^!,\cA^!)\bigr)^\vee
\otimes \omega_X.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Construction of~$c_{\cA}$.}\;
The factorization bimodule $\cA^{\mathrm{diag}}$ is
$\cA$~viewed as a factorization module over itself via the chiral
product $\mu\colon j_*j^*(\cA\boxtimes\cA)\to\Delta_*\cA$
(Chapter~\textup{\ref{ch:algebraic-foundations}}).
A factorization cochain
$\phi\in\mathrm{Hom}_{\operatorname{Fact}(X)}(\cA,\cA^{\mathrm{diag}})$
of Ran-depth~$n+2$ is a section over the open stratum
$C_{n+2}(X)\subset X^{n+2}$ that intertwines the chiral
multiplications at all~$n+2$ marked points. Restricting along the
diagonal embedding
$\Delta\colon\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)\hookrightarrow
\operatorname{Ran}_{n+2}(X)$ and descending to the FM model yields
a cochain
$c_{\cA}(\phi)\in
\Gamma(\overline{C}_{n+2}(X),
j_*j^*\cA^{\boxtimes(n+2)}\otimes\Omega^n_{\overline{C}_{n+2}}(\log D))$
which respects the three-component differential
$d_{\mathrm{Hoch}} = d_{\mathrm{int}}+d_{\mathrm{fact}}+d_{\mathrm{config}}$
(Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chiral-hochschild-differential}}):
the three pieces match, respectively, the $\mathcal{D}_X$-structure
on~$\cA$, the factorization-bimodule structure, and the de~Rham
differential on $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
Naturality is used only for morphisms of chiral algebras equipped
with compatible diagonal-bimodule maps; unrestricted covariance of
Hochschild cochains in the algebra variable is not asserted.

\emph{Part~(a): chain-level qualification.}\;
The $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$-structure on
$\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)$ is defined by a
simplicial colimit over finite subsets of~$X$
(Francis--Gaitsgory~\textup{\cite[Definition~5.5.2.1]{HA}}):
the differential contains boundary contributions
$\partial_{\mathrm{Ran}}$ that are simplicial-like. The FM model
$\overline{C}_{n+2}(X)$ replaces the Ran-simplicial structure by
a compactification, so the two differentials do not agree
on the nose: the boundary contributions from
$\partial_{\mathrm{Ran}}$ become logarithmic boundary residues in
the FM model. The two differentials agree only after passage to
the bar-degree spectral sequence, where the simplicial correction
terms are exact.
In explicit form: on bar degree~$n$, the two complexes differ by
exact terms of the form
$(\partial_{\mathrm{Ran}} - d_{\mathrm{config}})(\phi)
\in d_{\mathrm{int}}\cdot C^n_{\mathrm{chiral}}$, which are
$d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}$-boundaries but not zero.

\emph{Part~(b): cohomological isomorphism under diagonal descent.}\;
Filter $\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)$ by the
cardinality of the finite subset in the Ran presentation, and filter
the FM model of $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$ by collision depth. The
hypothesis identifies the associated-graded comparison with the
two-sided chiral bar resolution
\[
\operatorname{Bar}_{\cA^e}(\cA)
=\cA\otimes\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)\otimes\cA
\longrightarrow \cA
\]
from Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-bar-cobar}. On the PBW Koszul locus,
Proposition~\ref{prop:fm-tower-collapse} kills the positive
Arnold-fibre classes and leaves exactly the curve-level
$\cD_X$-Ext terms of Lemma~\ref{lem:hochschild-shift-computation}.
Thus the two filtered spectral sequences have isomorphic
$E_2$-pages and both degenerate at~$E_2$. The comparison
$c_{\cA}$ is therefore a quasi-isomorphism on cohomology. The
cohomology amplitude bound $\{0,1,2\}$ transfers from
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}.

\emph{Part~(c): $(\infty,1)$-enhancement.}\;
In the $(\infty,1)$-category $\mathrm{D}(\mathrm{Fact}(X))$,
filtered quasi-isomorphisms are equivalences. Part~(b) gives such a
filtered quasi-isomorphism exactly under the diagonal descent
hypothesis. Without that hypothesis the Francis--Gaitsgory internal
Hom and the FM totalization remain two different chain models linked
by the morphism~$c_{\cA}$, not by an asserted equality.

\emph{Part~(d): class dependence.}\;
Heisenberg $\mathcal{H}_k$
\textup{(}Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:free-fields}}\textup{)},
affine Kac--Moody $V_k(\mathfrak{g})$ at non-critical
level~\textup{\cite[Theorem~3.4.11]{BD04}},
$\beta\gamma$
\textup{(}Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:beta-gamma}}\textup{)},
and Virasoro $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ on the raw bounded universal lane
\textup{(}including $c=0$\textup{)}
all satisfy the PBW chiral Koszul hypothesis
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:chiral-koszul-pair}}\textup{)}
on the indicated lanes, and in these bounded models the
two-sided bar resolution gives the required diagonal Ran--FM descent.
The critical-level exclusion $k=-h^\vee$ follows from
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:critical-level-dimensional-divergence}}:
both sides of the comparison diverge there.
Class~M at $c=0$ is \emph{not} excluded from the comparison:
while the complementarity invariant $\kappa+\kappa^!$ has its
class-M ambient subtleties
\textup{(}class-M raw vs weight-completed ambient
discipline;
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:critical-level-dimensional-divergence}}
on the independent critical-level issue\textup{)}, the Koszul
duality datum is intact at $c=0$ on the raw bounded direct-sum
ambient, so
$\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\mathrm{Vir}_0,\mathrm{Vir}_0)
\cong \ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathrm{Vir}_0)$ holds.

\emph{Part~(e): Verdier self-duality intertwining.}\;
Verdier compatibility of the diagonal descent comparison says that
the square formed by $c_{\cA}$, $c_{\cA^!}$, and curve-level Verdier
duality commutes in cohomology. Theorem~\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}
then gives
\[
\ChirHoch^n(\cA)
\cong
\ChirHoch^{2-n}(\cA^!)^\vee\otimes\omega_X,
\]
and part~(b) transports this isomorphism across the two comparison
maps. This proves the displayed BD-side duality under precisely the
Verdier-compatible descent hypothesis.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Two distinct lanes both load-bearing]
\label{rem:bd-fact-chirhoch-two-lanes}
\index{factorization cohomology!two lanes}
The chain-level chiral lane and the $(\infty,1)$-categorical
BD/Francis--Gaitsgory lane are both load-bearing.
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bd-fact-vs-chirhoch}} is therefore stated
on two levels, both under the diagonal Ran--FM descent hypothesis.
Part~(b) is a $1$-categorical cohomological
statement (isomorphism of graded $\mathcal{D}_X$-modules),
used by the rest of this chapter and by
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:higher-genus}} wherever the
$\mathcal{D}_X$-Ext model is invoked. Part~(c) is the
$(\infty,1)$-categorical statement after filtered descent, used by
the thick-BD / Ran-derived enhancements in
Chapter~\textup{\ref{chap:higher-genus}} and by the
topological-factorization comparisons in Volume~II
(Vol~II Chapter on SC$^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ coproducts).
Both lanes are load-bearing: downgrading to
$1$-categorical alone loses the Francis--Gaitsgory
$(\infty,1)$-structure; demanding chain-level equivalence in
the $1$-categorical ambient is false
(Part~(a)).
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Theorem~H transported along diagonal factorization
descent;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{cor:thm-H-bd-extension}
\index{Theorem H!BD extension}
On the Koszul locus, whenever the diagonal Ran--FM descent and
Verdier-compatibility hypotheses of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bd-fact-vs-chirhoch}} hold, the Theorem~H
concentration
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}}\textup{)}
and Koszul reflection
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:main-koszul-hoch}}\textup{)}
both transport from $\ChirHoch^\bullet$ to
$\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $H^n(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA))=0$
for $n\notin\{0,1,2\}$;
\item $H^n(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA))
\cong H^{2-n}(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA^!,\cA^!))^\vee
\otimes\omega_X$;
\item the Hochschild--Hilbert polynomial
$P^{\mathrm{fact}}_{\cA}(t)
:=\sum_n \dim H^n(\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA))\,t^n$
satisfies the palindromic identity
$P^{\mathrm{fact}}_{\cA}(t) = t^2 P^{\mathrm{fact}}_{\cA^!}(t^{-1})$,
identical to the $\ChirHoch$-side palindromy.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bd-fact-vs-chirhoch}}\textup{(b, e)}
and Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Cross-volume: Vol II topological factorization]
\label{rem:vol2-topological-factorization-comparison}
\index{cross-volume!Vol II SC$^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ coproducts}
Volume~II defines the topological factorization algebra
$\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ and identifies its bar differential
with holomorphic factorization and its coproduct with topological
factorization (Vol~II Parts~I--VII, with the cross-volume scope
discipline recorded there). When the diagonal comparison of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:bd-fact-vs-chirhoch}}(c) is available, the
$(\infty,1)$-enhancement $\mathcal{C}^\bullet_{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA,\cA)\simeq
RHH_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ intertwines the Vol~II
$\mathrm{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-coproduct on the BD side with the
brace coproduct on the chiral Hochschild side
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chiral-deligne-tamarkin}}\textup{)}.
The Vol~I $\leftrightarrow$ Vol~II compatibility therefore rests on
this diagonal comparison, not on a bare identification of arbitrary
factorization cohomology with $\ChirHoch$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What~$E_2$-formality adds beyond Theorem~H]
\label{rem:e2-formality-vs-thmH}
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth} gives concentration.
Proposition~\ref{prop:e2-formality-hochschild} is a strictly stronger
conditional statement: the $\Etwo$-algebra structure on
$H^*(\ChirHoch(\cA))$ is determined by the cup product and the
Gerstenhaber bracket alone. The secondary Borcherds
operations $F_n$ from the homotopy chiral algebra structure on
$\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cech-hca}, Pillar~A) are exact for
$n \geq 3$ only after the brace-compatible contraction named in
Proposition~\ref{prop:e2-formality-hochschild} is supplied. PBW
concentration alone does not imply $\Etwo$-formality.

The converse ($\Etwo$-formality implies Koszulness) is false.
A non-Koszul algebra whose Hochschild cohomology happens
to concentrate in three degrees need not be $\Etwo$-formal:
concentration is only a support bound, while formality requires a
brace-compatible contraction. A stronger converse requires
the scalar-orbit formality problem discussed
below, for which no converse is proved here
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:convolution-formality-one-channel}}\textup{)}.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Scalar universal class implies convolution
formality along its distinguished orbit;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:convolution-formality-one-channel}
\index{formality!convolution algebra}
\index{one-channel!scalar-orbit formality problem}
\index{scalar saturation|see{one-channel}}
Let $\cA$ be a modular Koszul chiral algebra.
The modular convolution algebra
\[
\gAmod
\;=\;
\prod_{g,n}\,
\operatorname{Hom}_{\Sigma_n}\!\bigl(
 C_*(\overline{\cM}_{g,n}),\;
 \operatorname{End}_{\cA}(n)
\bigr)
\]
carries the five-component differential
$D = d_{\mathrm{int}} + [\tau,-] + d_{\mathrm{sew}}
 + d_{\mathrm{pf}} + \hbar\Delta$
and the universal Maurer--Cartan element
$\Theta_{\cA} := D_{\cA} - d_0
\in \MC(\gAmod)$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic})}.
Assume the full universal Maurer--Cartan element is scalar:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:one-channel-formality}
\Theta_{\cA}
\;=\;
\kappa(\cA) \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda.
\end{equation}
Then the quantum $L_\infty$-structure is formal along the
distinguished scalar Maurer--Cartan orbit of\/~$\Theta_{\cA}$:
the higher transferred brackets vanish on the one-dimensional
scalar line $\mathbb{C}\!\cdot\!\eta \otimes \Lambda$, and the MC
equation restricts there to the scalar genus identities.
No converse is proved here. In particular, one-channel
minimal-model concentration
$\Theta_{\cA}^{\min} = \eta \otimes \Gamma_{\cA}$ does
\emph{not} by itself imply the scalar identity
\eqref{eq:one-channel-formality}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Throughout this proof we write $\kappa$ for $\kappa(\cA)$.
Suppose $\Theta_{\cA} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:operadic-complexity-detailed},
one-channel forces shadow depth $r_{\max}(\cA) = 2$,
hence $A_\infty$-depth $d_\infty(\cA) = 2$ and
$L_\infty$-formality level $f_\infty(\cA) = 2$.
The genus-$0$ transferred $L_\infty$ brackets therefore
satisfy $\ell_k^{(0),\mathrm{tr}} = 0$ for $k \geq 3$:
the genus-$0$ convolution algebra is formal.

For the full scalar orbit, the shadow
obstruction tower terminates at degree~$2$:
$\Theta_{\cA}^{(\le r)} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$
for all~$r$. The obstruction classes
$o^{(r+1)}(\cA) \in H^2(F^{r+1}\gAmod / F^{r+2}\gAmod, d_2)$
vanish for all $r \geq 2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-all-degree-master-equation}).
Since the genus-$g$ quantum brackets $\ell_k^{(g)}$ for
$g \geq 1$ are induced by sewing on $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$,
and sewing applied to the scalar element
$\kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$ produces the scalar
genus-$g$ curvature $\kappa^g \cdot \eta_g \otimes \Lambda_g$
(which lies in the image of the differential, not in
independent cohomology), the transferred higher-genus brackets
$\ell_k^{(g),\mathrm{tr}}$ also vanish for $k \geq 3$.
This gives formality of the distinguished scalar orbit of
$\Theta_{\cA}$ inside~$\gAmod$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scalar-orbit formality and scalar saturation]
\label{rem:convolution-formality-cg}
\index{Chriss--Ginzburg principle!convolution formality}
\emph{Forward direction} (writing $\kappa$ for $\kappa(\cA)$).\;
If $\Theta_{\cA} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$, the
MC equation $D \Theta + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta, \Theta] = 0$
reduces to a scalar identity at each $(g,n)$:
$[\eta \otimes \Lambda, \eta \otimes \Lambda]$ factors through the
metric contraction, so the higher $L_\infty$-brackets $\ell_k$
($k \geq 3$) act trivially on
$\bC \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$. Hence
$\gAmod$ is formal along the orbit of~$\Theta_{\cA}$.

\emph{Converse / open direction.}\;
Current methods do \emph{not} show that formality of the full
quantum $L_\infty$-algebra forces scalar saturation, nor that
one-channelity alone implies formality. The strongest proved
input is the one-channel minimal-model statement
$\Theta_{\cA}^{\min}=\eta\otimes\Gamma_{\cA}$
\textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:scalar-saturation}}\textup{)};
identifying $\Gamma_{\cA}$ with
$\kappa(\cA)\Lambda$ is the open tautological-purity step outside
the proved scalar lane.

\emph{Relation to the shadow obstruction tower.}\;
The non-scalar universal classes
of~\S\ref{subsec:non-scalar-theta} measure the deviation of
$\Theta_{\cA}$ from the scalar line. The cubic shadow~$C$, quartic resonance class~$Q$,
and all higher shadows $\mathrm{Sh}_r$ are the
\emph{obstructions to formality}: the higher-order
corrections preventing $\Theta_{\cA}$ from lying on the
scalar line.

\emph{Pillar~C interaction} (Mok~\cite{Mok25}):
the planted-forest coefficient algebra $G_{\mathrm{pf}}$
(Definition~\ref{def:planted-forest-coefficient-algebra}) controls
the non-formal corrections. Vanishing planted-forest
contributions removes one source of deviation from the scalar
orbit, but no converse criterion for full convolution formality
is proved here
(Remark~\ref{rem:full-homotopy-why}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Hierarchy: Koszulness, modular Koszulness, formality]
\label{rem:formality-vs-koszul}
Three properties of increasing strength:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Koszulness} (genus~$0$): the bar spectral sequence
 collapses at~$E_2$
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration}).

\item \emph{Modular Koszulness} (all genera): MK3 extends PBW
 collapse; the scalar trace $\kappa(\cA)$ is the sole survivor
 in the modular bar cohomology at $g \geq 1$.

\item \emph{Scalar-orbit convolution formality} (structural, on the
 proved scalar lane): when the full universal class is scalar,
 the quantum $L_\infty$-structure is formal along its
 distinguished scalar orbit, by
 Theorem~\ref{thm:convolution-formality-one-channel}.
\end{enumerate}
On the proved scalar lane, the implication
$\text{(c)} \Rightarrow \text{(b)} \Rightarrow \text{(a)}$
holds. Outside that lane, the first converse-type problem is
exactly the non-scalar shadow obstruction tower
(\S\ref{subsec:non-scalar-theta}); the second is the
higher-genus curvature.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[MC tangent amplitude on the Koszul locus;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{prop:mc-tangent-amplitude}
\index{Maurer--Cartan!tangent amplitude}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on a smooth projective curve~$X$
with universal MC element $\Theta_{\cA} \in \MC(\gAmod)$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic})}.
If $\cA$ is PBW chiral Koszul and satisfies the same completion
hypotheses as Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}},
then the curve-level tangent complex at $\Theta_{\cA}$ has amplitude
\[
H^n\!\bigl(\gAmod,\operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA})\bigr)=0
\qquad(n\geq 3)
\]
in the Vol~I chiral Hochschild lane. Smoothness of the MC moduli at
$\Theta_{\cA}$ is a separate Kuranishi condition: after passing to a
minimal $L_\infty$ model on
$H^\bullet(\gAmod,\operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA}))$, it is equivalent
to vanishing of the obstruction maps
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mc-smoothness}
\kappa_m\colon
\operatorname{Sym}^m H^1\!\bigl(\gAmod,\operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA})\bigr)
\longrightarrow
H^2\!\bigl(\gAmod,\operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA})\bigr),
\qquad m\geq2,
\end{equation}
not to vanishing of $H^2$ itself.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The twisted tangent complex at $\Theta_{\cA}$ is the convolution
complex $\bigl(\gAmod,\operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA})\bigr)$.
On the Vol~I curve-level Hochschild summand, the identification with
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\cA)$ is the shadow projection of
Proposition~\ref{prop:hochschild-shadow-projection}. The PBW chiral
Koszul and completion hypotheses are precisely those of
Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}; hence the
curve-level summand has no cohomology in degrees~$\geq3$.

The final assertion is the standard deformation theory of a dg Lie,
or more generally $L_\infty$, algebra. Passing to a minimal model
transfers the brackets to cohomology. The formal moduli functor is
smooth at the base point exactly when the transferred Kuranishi
obstruction maps from $H^1$ to $H^2$ vanish. The vector space $H^2$
is the target of obstructions, not the obstruction itself: the
Heisenberg level line below gives a nonzero $H^2$ with an
unobstructed one-parameter family.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Identifying the obstruction space]
\label{rem:mc-smoothness-pbw}
The twisted cohomology
$H^2(\gAmod, \operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA}))$ admits a direct
identification.
At genus~$0$, the $(g,n) = (0,3)$ component of the
$\operatorname{ad}(\Theta_{\cA})$-twisted complex is
$\ChirHoch^2(\cA)$
(Corollary~\ref{cor:def-obs-exchange-genus0}), and for a
Koszul algebra this equals
$Z(\cA^!)^\vee \otimes \omega_X$: a finite-dimensional space
completely controlled by the Koszul dual.

At genus~$g \geq 1$, the contributions come from the modular bar
complex. The modular Koszulness axiom MK3 forces the bar spectral
sequence to collapse at~$E_1$ in the bidegrees governed by
Theorem~H, which removes cohomology above the curve-level window but
does not force the degree-$2$ obstruction space to vanish.
The shadow obstruction tower
(Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-extraction}) then determines
$\Theta_{\cA}$ from~$\kappa(\cA)$ on the scalar lane.

The Heisenberg algebra shows why $H^2=0$ is the wrong smoothness
criterion: $H^2=\bC$ is the level-deformation line, and the resulting
one-parameter family is unobstructed. The obstruction is the
Kuranishi map into this line, not the line itself. A converse theorem
recovering Koszulness from MC smoothness must prove that
every non-collapsing class in the bar spectral sequence produces a
nonzero Kuranishi map~\eqref{eq:mc-smoothness}.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Bifunctor obstruction decomposition;
\ClaimStatusConditional]
\label{thm:bifunctor-obstruction-decomposition}%
\index{bifunctor obstruction!decomposition}
\index{Robert-Nicoud--Wierstra!no-bifunctor obstruction}
The convolution $sL_\infty$-algebra
$\operatorname{hom}_\alpha(\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA),\, \cA)$
is functorial in each slot separately but fails as a bifunctor
\textup{(\cite{RNW19}, Theorem~6.6;
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:two-level-convention})}}.
For a chirally Koszul algebra~$\cA$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The degree-$3$ obstruction class
\[
\mathrm{obs}_3
\;\in\;
H^2\!\bigl(
 \operatorname{hom}_\alpha^{(3)}
 (\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA),\, \cA)
\bigr)
\]
is nonzero in general, but is immaterial for the MC3 categorical
lift: Koszulness makes one-slot factorization sufficient.

\item Every two-sided $\infty$-morphism that fails to exist as a
 bifunctor morphism decomposes as a one-sided coalgebra morphism
 followed by a one-sided algebra morphism, with the composition
 independent of ordering up to homotopy.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(i): the obstruction class $\mathrm{obs}_3$ is the failure of
$\operatorname{hom}_\alpha$ to extend to $\infty$-morphisms in both
slots simultaneously (\cite{RNW19}, Theorem~6.6). For chirally
Koszul~$\cA$, the bar-cobar counit
$\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism;
the one-slot convention
(Remark~\ref{rem:two-level-convention}) fixes the cooperad slot and
varies the algebra by $\infty$-morphisms. The bar-cobar inversion
gives a canonical strict model, so both-slot variation is
unnecessary: the MC3 categorical lift proceeds one slot at a time
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc3-type-a-resolution}).

Part~(ii): a two-sided $\infty$-morphism $(f, g)$ with $f$ on the
coalgebra side and $g$ on the algebra side satisfies
$\partial f + f \star g = 0$; by the one-slot convention, this
factors as $f$~followed by~$g$ with the composition determined up
to homotopy by the contractibility of the space of
$\infty$-morphisms between quasi-isomorphic objects.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Heisenberg test case and the MC3 frontier]
\label{rem:bifunctor-analysis}
\emph{Testability.}\;
For the Heisenberg algebra $\cH_k$, the obstruction
$\mathrm{obs}_3$ lives in the two-dimensional space
$H^2(\operatorname{hom}_\alpha^{(3)}
 (\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k), \cH_k))$.
An explicit computation: $\barB^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cH_k)$ is
concentrated in bar degree~$1$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-concentration}),
so $\operatorname{hom}_\alpha^{(3)}$ reduces to maps from
the triple self-product of the cogenerators. The obstruction is
the failure of the Leibniz rule for the simultaneous
coalgebra-algebra functoriality, which is nonzero even for this
simplest example because the Koszul duality functor itself is
not strict-monoidal.

\emph{Structural origin.}\;
The no-bifunctor theorem of~\cite{RNW19} (\S6) is universal:
$\mathrm{obs}_3 \neq 0$ for \emph{any} cooperad-operad pair.
The content of part~(ii) is that Koszulness provides a
\emph{one-slot workaround}: the Quillen equivalence
$\Omega_\kappa \dashv \barB_\kappa$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:quillen-equivalence-chiral})
transports $\infty$-morphisms through one slot at a time.
This is why the MC3 resolution
(Theorem~\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}, Corollary~\ref{cor:mc3-all-types}) succeeds: each step
on the proved all-types surface
\textup{(}categorical prefundamental Clebsch--Gordan via
multiplicity-free $\ell$-weights together with the generated-core DK
comparison\textup{)} is a one-slot operation. The later chromatic,
completion, and compact-extension steps belong to the separate
post-CG packet, reduced in type~$A$ but not proved in all types.
The all-types generalization therefore proceeds one slot at a time on
the evaluation-generated core; the decomposition property of
part~(ii) explains why this is sufficient on that proved surface.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Operadic inheritance of Koszulness]
\label{rem:operadic-inheritance}
\index{Koszulness!operadic inheritance}
The descent of chiral Koszulness from Koszulness of the chiral
operad $P^{\mathrm{ch}}$ is a separate theorem, not an implicit
consequence of Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-chiral-koszul-duality}. Its proof
requires formality of $\overline{\mathrm{FM}}_n(X)$ as operadic
objects on curves and the transfer statement recorded in
Theorem~\ref{thm:operadic-complexity}; the associative case is the
one-slot specialization implemented by
Lemma~\ref{lem:operadic-koszul-transfer}.
\end{remark}

\section{Example: boson-fermion duality}

\subsection{The free boson chiral algebra}

The free boson $\mathcal{B} = \mathcal{H}_k$ at level~$k$ on a curve $X$ is defined as follows:

\emph{As a chiral algebra.}
The free boson $\mathcal{B}$ is the chiral envelope of the Heisenberg Lie$^*$ algebra
$\omega_X$ (with Lie$^*$ bracket given by the residue pairing). Its vacuum module is
$\mathrm{Sym}(\omega_X \otimes t^{-1}\mathbb{C}[t^{-1}])$, a polynomial algebra on
infinitely many generators $\alpha_{-n}$ ($n \geq 1$).

\emph{Generator.} The field $\alpha(z)$ generates $\mathcal{B}$ with conformal weight $h = 1$.

\emph{Chiral multiplication.} Determined by the OPE
\[
\alpha(z_1) \alpha(z_2) = \frac{k}{(z_1-z_2)^2} + \text{regular}
\]

In terms of modes $\alpha(z) = \sum_{n \in \mathbb{Z}} \alpha_n z^{-n-1}$:
\[
[\alpha_m, \alpha_n] = k \cdot m \delta_{m+n,0}
\]
The central charge is $c = 1$ (at level $k = 1$; in general $c = 1$ for any~$k$, since the Heisenberg algebra has $c = 1$ independent of level).

\emph{Vacuum representation.} The Fock space
\[
\mathcal{F}_{\mathcal{B}} = \mathbb{C}[\alpha_{-1}, \alpha_{-2}, \ldots] |0\rangle
\]
with $\alpha_n |0\rangle = 0$ for $n \geq 0$.

\subsection{The free fermion chiral algebra}

The free fermion $\mathcal{F}$ has:

\emph{Generators.} Two fermionic fields $\psi(z), \psi^*(z)$ with $h = 1/2$.

\emph{Relations.} The OPEs
\begin{align}
\psi(z_1)\psi^*(z_2) &= \frac{1}{z_1-z_2} + \text{regular} \\
\psi(z_1)\psi(z_2) &= 0 + \text{regular} \\
\psi^*(z_1)\psi^*(z_2) &= 0 + \text{regular}
\end{align}

In modes (half-integer for Neveu--Schwarz sector):
\begin{align}
\{\psi_r, \psi^*_s\} &= \delta_{r+s,0} \\
\{\psi_r, \psi_s\} &= 0 \\
\{\psi^*_r, \psi^*_s\} &= 0
\end{align}

\emph{Fock space.}
\[
\mathcal{F}_{\mathcal{F}} = \Lambda^{\bullet}(\psi_{-1/2}, \psi_{-3/2}, \ldots, \psi^*_{-1/2}, \psi^*_{-3/2}, \ldots) |0\rangle
\]

\subsection{Boson-fermion correspondence as lattice VOA extension, not Koszul duality}

\begin{theorem}[Boson-fermion correspondence via lattice VOA; \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere{} \cite{FK80}]\label{thm:boson-fermion-lattice}
The free boson $\mathcal{B}$ and free fermion $\mathcal{F}$ are related by bosonization through the rank-1 lattice vertex algebra $V_{\mathbb{Z}}$:
\[
V_{\mathbb{Z}} \supset \mathcal{B}, \qquad \mathcal{F} \cong V_{\mathbb{Z}} \quad \text{(as super vertex algebras)}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}
This is \emph{not} Koszul duality in the operadic sense (Remark~\ref{rem:bosonization-not-koszul}). Koszul duality preserves the dimension of the generating space: if $\mathcal{A}$ has generators in a space $V$, then $\mathcal{A}^!$ has generators in $V^*$, so $\dim V = \dim V^*$. Here $\mathcal{B}$ has one generator ($\alpha$) while $\mathcal{F}$ has two generators ($\psi, \psi^*$). The Heisenberg algebra is \emph{not} Koszul self-dual: $\mathcal{H}_\kappa^! \simeq \mathrm{Sym}^{ch}(V^*)$, a commutative chiral algebra (Part~\ref{part:bar-cobar-engine}, the characteristic-datum apparatus). The boson-fermion correspondence is instead a lattice VOA extension: the vertex operators $\psi = {:}e^{i\phi}{:}$ and $\psi^* = {:}e^{-i\phi}{:}$ lie in $V_{\mathbb{Z}}$, not in the Heisenberg subalgebra.
\end{remark}

\begin{proof}
The argument has three levels:

\emph{Level 1: The Lattice Extension}

The free boson $\mathcal{B}$ is generated by $\alpha(z) = i\partial\phi(z)$ with OPE $\alpha(z)\alpha(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2$. The rank-1 lattice VOA $V_{\mathbb{Z}}$ extends $\mathcal{B}$ by adjoining vertex operators $e^{in\phi}$ for $n \in \mathbb{Z}$:
\[
V_{\mathbb{Z}} = \bigoplus_{n \in \mathbb{Z}} \mathcal{F}_n, \qquad \mathcal{F}_n = \mathcal{B} \cdot {:}e^{in\phi}{:}
\]
The charge-$(\pm 1)$ sectors produce the fermionic fields $\psi = {:}e^{i\phi}{:}$ and $\psi^* = {:}e^{-i\phi}{:}$.

\emph{Level 2: Bosonization}

The explicit isomorphism is given by bosonization:
\begin{align}
\psi(z) &= :e^{i\phi(z)}: \\
\psi^*(z) &= :e^{-i\phi(z)}: \\
\alpha(z) &= i\partial\phi(z)
\end{align}

where $\phi$ is the bosonic field with $\phi(z)\phi(w) \sim -\log(z-w)$.

This realizes the isomorphism at the level of vertex operators:
\[
Y_{\mathcal{F}}(\psi, z) = :e^{i\int^z \alpha}: \quad \text{(fermion as exponential of boson)}
\]

\emph{Level 3: Bar Complex of the Heisenberg}

The bar complex of $\mathcal{B}$ has underlying space:
\[
\overline{B}^{\text{ch}}(\mathcal{B}) = \text{span}\{[\alpha^{n_1}]|[\alpha^{n_2}]|\cdots|[\alpha^{n_k}]\}
\]

with coproduct:
\[
\Delta([\alpha^n]) = \sum_{i+j=n} [\alpha^i] \otimes [\alpha^j]
\]

This is the divided power coalgebra $\Gamma(V^*)$, which is the Koszul dual \emph{coalgebra}. Its linear dual is the symmetric algebra $\mathrm{Sym}(V)$, and the Koszul dual \emph{algebra} is $\mathcal{H}_\kappa^! \simeq \mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ (Part~\ref{part:bar-cobar-engine}, the characteristic-datum apparatus), confirming that the Heisenberg algebra is Koszul (Theorem~\ref{thm:km-chiral-koszul}) but \emph{not} Koszul self-dual. (The cobar $\Omega(\bar{B}(\mathcal{H}_\kappa))$ recovers $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ itself.)
\end{proof}

\subsection{Boson and fermion chiral Hochschild cohomologies and their non-Koszul comparison}

\begin{computation}[Boson chiral Hochschild cohomology; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:boson-hochschild}

\emph{Degree 0.}
\[
\ChirHoch^0(\mathcal{B}) = Z(\mathcal{B})
\]
the center of $\mathcal{B}$, consisting of elements whose OPE with every field is regular.
An element $a \in \mathcal{B}$ lies in the center if and only if $a(z)\alpha(w) \sim 0$ (no singular terms). Since $\alpha(z)\alpha(w) \sim k(z-w)^{-2}$, the only such elements are scalars. Thus $\ChirHoch^0 = \mathbb{C}$.

\emph{Degree 1.}
A chiral derivation $D: \mathcal{B} \to \mathcal{B}$ must satisfy the Leibniz rule for the $\lambda$-bracket: $D(\{\alpha_\lambda \alpha\}) = \{D(\alpha)_\lambda \alpha\} + \{\alpha_\lambda D(\alpha)\}$.
Since $\{\alpha_\lambda \alpha\} = \kappa\lambda$ is a scalar, the left side is $0$, and the constraint is $\{D(\alpha)_\lambda \alpha\} + \{\alpha_\lambda D(\alpha)\} = 0$.
The derivation $D(\alpha) = c \cdot \mathbf{1}$ (a scalar) satisfies this because $\{c_\lambda \alpha\} = 0$ and $\{\alpha_\lambda c\} = 0$.
It is outer. An inner chiral derivation by a field~$a$ acts on
$\alpha$ as $a_{(0)}\alpha$. The Heisenberg zero mode is central:
$[\alpha_0,\alpha_n]=0$ for all~$n$, hence
$\alpha_{(0)}\alpha=0$ and $\mathbf{1}_{(0)}\alpha=0$. No field
$a\in\mathcal B$ has $a_{(0)}\alpha=\mathbf1$.
Thus $\ChirHoch^1 = \mathbb{C}$, generated by the outer derivation $D(\alpha) = \mathbf{1}$.

\emph{Degree 2.}
A 2-cocycle $\phi \in C^2$ defines a deformation:
\[
\alpha(z) \cdot_t \alpha(w) = \alpha(z)\alpha(w) + t\phi(z,w)
\]
The cocycle condition ensures associativity to first order. The space of such cocycles
is one-dimensional, spanned by the level deformation $\alpha(z) \alpha(w) \sim k/(z-w)^2 \mapsto (k + \epsilon t)/(z-w)^2$. Thus $\ChirHoch^2 = \mathbb{C}$.
\end{computation}

\begin{computation}[Fermion chiral Hochschild cohomology; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:fermion-hochschild}

The fermion case differs from the boson in one key respect: the OPE $\psi(z)\psi^*(w) \sim 1/(z-w)$ produces a simple pole (not a double pole), so the bar differential acts on degree-$1$ generators by residue extraction rather than by the second-order Casimir. The Hochschild computation then parallels the bosonic case with the quadratic Casimir $\kappa/(z-w)^2$ replaced by the identity pairing $1/(z-w)$.

\emph{Degree~$0$.} The center $Z(\mathcal{F})$ consists of elements with regular OPE against both $\psi$ and $\psi^*$. Since $\psi(z)\psi^*(w) \sim (z-w)^{-1}$, only scalars commute with all generators, giving $\ChirHoch^0 = \mathbb{C}$.

\emph{Degree~$1$.} All derivations of the Clifford algebra are inner \cite[Ch.~9]{Weibel94}, so $\ChirHoch^1 = 0$.

\emph{Degree~$2$.} The unique deformation is the level shift $\psi(z)\psi^*(w) \sim (1+\epsilon t)/(z-w)$, giving $\ChirHoch^2 = \mathbb{C}$.
\begin{align}
\ChirHoch^0(\mathcal{F}) &= \mathbb{C} \quad \text{(scalars only)} \\
\ChirHoch^1(\mathcal{F}) &= 0 \quad \text{(rigid)} \\
\ChirHoch^2(\mathcal{F}) &= \mathbb{C} \quad \text{(level deformation)}
\end{align}
The fermion Hochschild groups differ from the boson groups at degree~$1$: $\ChirHoch^1(\mathcal{F}) = 0$ (all chiral derivations are inner) while $\ChirHoch^1(\mathcal{B}) = \mathbb{C}$ (Computation~\ref{comp:boson-hochschild}). The two algebras are \emph{not} Koszul dual (see Remark below).
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[Boson-fermion chiral Hochschild comparison: pole order controls innerness]
\label{rem:boson-fermion-hochschild-comparison}
The boson and fermion have \emph{non-isomorphic} chiral Hochschild cohomology:
\[
\ChirHoch^n(\mathcal{B}) = (\mathbb{C}, \mathbb{C}, \mathbb{C}), \qquad
\ChirHoch^n(\mathcal{F}) = (\mathbb{C}, 0, \mathbb{C}).
\]
The discrepancy at degree~$1$ reflects the \emph{pole order} of the OPE. For the fermion, $\psi(z)\psi^*(w) \sim (z-w)^{-1}$ has a simple pole, so $\psi_{(0)}\psi^* = 1$ is nontrivial; inner derivations span all of $\mathrm{Der}(\mathcal{F})$. For the boson, $\alpha(z)\alpha(w) \sim k(z-w)^{-2}$ has no simple pole, so $\alpha_{(0)}\alpha = 0$; the outer derivation $D(\alpha) = \mathbf{1}$ survives. In general:
\begin{center}
\emph{Simple pole in the OPE $\Longrightarrow$ nontrivial zero mode $\Longrightarrow$ inner derivation.}\\
\emph{No simple pole $\Longrightarrow$ central zero mode $\Longrightarrow$ outer derivation survives.}
\end{center}
The boson and fermion are \emph{not} Koszul dual: the Heisenberg has one generator
while the fermion has two, and the bosonization correspondence is an \emph{isomorphism} via lattice VOA extension, not a Koszul duality. The Koszul dual of $\mathcal{H}_k$ is $\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ with curvature $m_0 = -k\omega$ (equivalently, $\mathrm{CE}(\mathfrak{h}_{-k})$ since $\mathfrak{h}$ is abelian), not $\mathcal{F}$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The cyclic deformation complex}
\label{subsec:cyclic-deformation}

\begin{definition}[Cyclic deformation complex: elementary models]
\label{def:cyclic-deformation-elementary}
\index{cyclic deformation complex|textbf}
\index{Def cyc@$\operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}$|textbf}
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on~$X$. The homotopy-invariant
\emph{cyclic deformation object} of~$\cA$ is a complete filtered cyclic
$L_\infty$-algebra controlling cyclic deformations of~$\cA$.
A strict presentation is the
\emph{cyclic deformation complex} $\Defcyc(\cA)$
used for calculations below.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{Abstract definition (H-level).}
$\operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)$ is the Lie algebra object in
the $\infty$-category of cochain complexes whose Maurer--Cartan
elements parametrize flat cyclic deformations of~$\cA$ over
Artinian bases. For the full construction, which requires a cyclic
$L_\infty$ algebra over the modular operad, see
Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-MC}.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{Concrete models (M-level).}
For the examples treated in this monograph, explicit models are:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Bar coderivations.}
 $\operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)_{\mathrm{bar}}
 := \operatorname{CoDer}^{\mathrm{cyc}}(\bar{B}_X(\cA))$,
 the complex of cyclic coderivations of the bar construction.
 Its Maurer--Cartan elements are exactly the curved deformations
 of the bar differential.
\item \emph{Cyclic chiral Hochschild complex.}
 $\operatorname{Def}_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\cA)_{\mathrm{Hoch}}
 := CC^*_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)^{\mathrm{cyc}}$,
 the cyclic-invariant part of the chiral Hochschild cochain complex
 (the complex controlling $S^1$-equivariant deformations).
\item \emph{Stable-graph operations.}
 For $\cA$ modular Koszul
 (Definition~\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral}), the genus-$g$
 deformations are generated by stable-graph operations
 $\gamma \in \Gamma_{g,n}$, and the Maurer--Cartan equation
 splits into genus-graded components whose leading term is the
 curvature $\mcurv{g} = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g$
 \textup{(UNIFORM-WEIGHT)}.
\end{enumerate}

The Heisenberg specialization (Chapter~\ref{ch:heisenberg-frame})
is computed via model~(a): the cyclic coderivation complex is
one-dimensional at genus~$1$, generated by the Eisenstein element
$\kappa \cdot E_2(\tau)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Quantum \texorpdfstring{$L_\infty$}{L-infinity} versus cyclic \texorpdfstring{$L_\infty$}{L-infinity}]
\label{rem:quantum-vs-cyclic-linf}
\index{quantum L-infinity algebra@quantum $L_\infty$ algebra|textbf}
\index{loop homotopy algebra|see{quantum $L_\infty$ algebra}}
Three levels arise as the genus filtration opens:
(i)~\emph{cyclic $L_\infty$} ($g = 0$, tree-level operations);
(ii)~\emph{quantum $L_\infty$} (all $g$; Braun--Lazarev~\cite{BL15},
Markl~\cite{Markl06}: operations $m^{(g)}_n$ on stable graphs
satisfying the QME $\sum_g \hbar^g m^{(g)} = 0$);
(iii)~\emph{modular homotopy type} (coupled to factorization on
$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$,
Definition~\ref{def:modular-homotopy-theory-intro}).
The lift (i)$\to$(ii) is obstructed by $\Delta(m_0)$ (unimodularity);
Koszul chiral algebras carry full modular homotopy types via
$\Theta_\cA$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-MC}).
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Genus-\texorpdfstring{$0$}{0} cyclic coderivation complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{prop:genus0-cyclic-coderivation}
\index{cyclic deformation complex!genus-$0$ construction}
Let $\cA$ be a Koszul chiral algebra with non-degenerate
invariant bilinear form
$\langle{-},{-}\rangle_{\cA}\colon \cA\otimes\cA\to\omega_X$.
Let $\bar{B}_X(\cA) = T^c(s^{-1}\bar{\cA})$ be the reduced bar
coalgebra
\textup{(}\S\textup{\ref{sec:bar-cobar}}\textup{)}.
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Cyclic coalgebra structure.}
